<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">World War II</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"The Second World War", "WWII", and "WW2" redirect here. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/The_Second_World_War_(disambiguation)" title="The Second World War (disambiguation)">The Second World War (disambiguation)</a> and <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/WWII_(disambiguation)" title="WWII (disambiguation)">WWII (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

(clockwise from top left)
<div class="hlist">
<ul>
<li>Chinese forces in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wanjialing" title="Battle of Wanjialing">Battle of Wanjialing</a></li>

<li>German <a href="/wiki/Junkers_Ju_87" title="Junkers Ju 87">Stuka</a> dive bombers on the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front</a> in December 1943</li>
<li>American naval force in the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Lingayen_Gulf" title="Invasion of Lingayen Gulf">Lingayen Gulf</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Keitel" title="Wilhelm Keitel">Wilhelm Keitel</a> signing the <a href="/wiki/German_Instrument_of_Surrender" title="German Instrument of Surrender">German Instrument of Surrender</a></li>
<li>Soviet troops in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad" title="Battle of Stalingrad">Battle of Stalingrad</a></li>
</ul>

<table style="width:100%;margin:0;padding:0;border:0">
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Date</th>
<td>1 September 1939 – 2 September 1945 <span style="display:none">(<span class="dtstart">1939-09-01</span> – <span class="dtend">1945-09-02</span>)</span> <span class="nowrap">(<span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7003219300000000000♠</span>6 years and 1 day)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[a]</a></sup></span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Location</th>
<td><span class="location"><a href="/wiki/European_theatre_of_World_War_II" title="European theatre of World War II">Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">Pacific</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Atlantic" title="Battle of the Atlantic">Atlantic</a>, <a href="/wiki/South-East_Asian_theatre_of_World_War_II" title="South-East Asian theatre of World War II">South-East Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_and_Middle_East_theatre_of_World_War_II" title="Mediterranean and Middle East theatre of World War II">Middle East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_and_Middle_East_theatre_of_World_War_II" title="Mediterranean and Middle East theatre of World War II">Mediterranean</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_African_Campaign" title="North African Campaign">North Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_African_Campaign_(World_War_II)" title="East African Campaign (World War II)">Horn of Africa</a>, briefly <a href="/wiki/American_Theater_(World_War_II)" title="American Theater (World War II)">North</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_River_Plate" title="Battle of the River Plate">South America</a></span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Result</th>
<td>
<p><a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> victory</p>
<ul>
<li>Collapse of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a></li>
<li>Fall of <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japanese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_Empire" title="Italian Empire">Italian Empires</a></li>
<li>Dissolution of the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a></li>
<li>Creation of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a></li>
<li>Emergence of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> as <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">superpowers</a></li>
<li>Beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> (<a href="/wiki/World_War_II#Aftermath" title="World War II">more...</a>)</li>
</ul>
</td>

<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:TopicTOC-World_War_II" title="Template:TopicTOC-World War II"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:TopicTOC-World_War_II" title="Template talk:TopicTOC-World War II"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:TopicTOC-World_War_II&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>

<p><b>World War II</b> (often abbreviated to <b>WWII</b> or <b>WW2</b>), also known as the <b>Second World War</b>, was a <a href="/wiki/World_war" title="World war">global war</a> that lasted from 1939 to 1945, although related conflicts began earlier. It involved <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_by_country" title="World War II by country">the vast majority of the world's countries</a>—including all of the <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">great powers</a>—eventually forming two opposing <a href="/wiki/Military_alliance" title="Military alliance">military alliances</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis</a>. It was the most widespread war in history, and directly involved more than 100 million people from over 30 countries. In a state of <a href="/wiki/Total_war" title="Total war">total war</a>, the major participants threw their entire economic, industrial, and scientific capabilities behind the <a href="/wiki/War_effort" title="War effort">war effort</a>, erasing the distinction between civilian and military resources.</p>
<p>World War II was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_wars_and_anthropogenic_disasters_by_death_toll" title="List of wars and anthropogenic disasters by death toll">deadliest conflict</a> in <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_world" title="History of the world">human history</a>, marked by 50 million to 85 million fatalities, most of which were civilians in the Soviet Union and China. It included <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Massacres" title="Massacres">massacres</a>, the deliberate genocide of <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>, <a href="/wiki/Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II" title="Strategic bombing during World War II">strategic bombing</a>, starvation, disease and the first use of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear weapons</a> in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert2001291_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert2001291-3">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESommerville2008p._5_.282011_ed..29_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESommerville2008p._5_.282011_ed..29-5">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a> aimed to dominate <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a> and was already <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">at war</a> with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%9349)" title="Republic of China (1912–49)">Republic of China</a> in 1937,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarrettShyu20016_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarrettShyu20016-7">[5]</a></sup> but the world war is generally said to have begun on 1 September 1939<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[6]</a></sup> with the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">invasion</a> of <a href="/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic" title="Second Polish Republic">Poland</a> by <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> and subsequent declarations of war on Germany by <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">France</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>. <a href="/wiki/German%E2%80%93Soviet_Commercial_Agreement_(1940)" title="German–Soviet Commercial Agreement (1940)">Supplied by the Soviet Union</a>, from late 1939 to early 1941, in a series of campaigns and <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Pact" title="Tripartite Pact">treaties</a>, Germany conquered or controlled much of continental Europe, and formed the Axis alliance with <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japan</a>. Under the <a href="/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact">Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact</a> of August 1939, Germany and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> partitioned and annexed territories of their European neighbours, <a href="/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Poland" title="Soviet invasion of Poland">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winter_War" title="Winter War">Finland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina" title="Soviet occupation of Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina">Romania</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Baltic_states" title="Occupation of the Baltic states">Baltic states</a>. The war continued primarily between the European Axis powers and the coalition of the United Kingdom and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">British Commonwealth</a>, with campaigns including the <a href="/wiki/Western_Desert_Campaign" title="Western Desert Campaign">North Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_African_Campaign_(World_War_II)" title="East African Campaign (World War II)">East Africa</a> campaigns, the aerial <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Britain" title="Battle of Britain">Battle of Britain</a>, the <a href="/wiki/The_Blitz" title="The Blitz">Blitz bombing campaign</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Campaign_(World_War_II)" title="Balkan Campaign (World War II)">Balkan Campaign</a> as well as the long-running <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Atlantic" title="Battle of the Atlantic">Battle of the Atlantic</a>. On 22 June 1941, the European Axis powers launched <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">an invasion of the Soviet Union</a>, opening the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">largest land theatre of war in history</a>, which trapped the major part of the Axis military forces into a <a href="/wiki/Attrition_warfare" title="Attrition warfare">war of attrition</a>. In December 1941, Japan <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attacked the United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Malaya" title="Japanese invasion of Malaya">European colonies</a> in the Pacific Ocean, and quickly conquered much of the Western Pacific.</p>
<p>The Axis advance halted in 1942 when Japan lost the critical <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Midway" title="Battle of Midway">Battle of Midway</a>, and Germany and Italy were defeated in <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_El_Alamein" title="Second Battle of El Alamein">North Africa</a> and then, decisively, at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad" title="Battle of Stalingrad">Stalingrad</a> in the Soviet Union. In 1943, with a series of German defeats on the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Sicily" title="Allied invasion of Sicily">Allied invasion of Sicily</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Italy" title="Allied invasion of Italy">Allied invasion of Italy</a> which brought about Italian surrender, and Allied victories in the Pacific, the Axis lost the initiative and undertook strategic retreat on all fronts. In 1944, the Western Allies <a href="/wiki/Normandy_landings" title="Normandy landings">invaded German-occupied France</a>, while the Soviet Union regained all of its territorial losses and invaded Germany and its allies. During 1944 and 1945 the Japanese suffered major reverses in mainland Asia in <a href="/wiki/Second_Guangxi_Campaign" title="Second Guangxi Campaign">South</a> <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_West_Hunan" title="Battle of West Hunan">Central China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burma_Campaign" title="Burma Campaign">Burma</a>, while the Allies crippled the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Navy" title="Imperial Japanese Navy">Japanese Navy</a> and captured key Western Pacific islands.</p>
<p>The war in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> concluded with an <a href="/wiki/Western_Allied_invasion_of_Germany" title="Western Allied invasion of Germany">invasion of Germany</a> by the Western Allies and the Soviet Union, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Berlin" title="Battle of Berlin">capture of Berlin</a> by Soviet troops, the <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Adolf_Hitler" title="Death of Adolf Hitler">suicide of Adolf Hitler</a> and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/German_Instrument_of_Surrender" title="German Instrument of Surrender">German unconditional surrender</a> on <a href="/wiki/Victory_in_Europe_Day" title="Victory in Europe Day">8 May 1945</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/Potsdam_Declaration" title="Potsdam Declaration">Potsdam Declaration</a> by the Allies on 26 July 1945 and the refusal of Japan to surrender under its terms, the United States <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">dropped atomic bombs</a> on the Japanese cities of <a href="/wiki/Hiroshima" title="Hiroshima">Hiroshima</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nagasaki" title="Nagasaki">Nagasaki</a> on 6 August and 9 August respectively. With an <a href="/wiki/Operation_Downfall" title="Operation Downfall">invasion of the Japanese archipelago</a> imminent, the possibility of additional atomic bombings and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria" title="Soviet invasion of Manchuria">Soviet invasion of Manchuria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">Japan formally surrendered</a> on 2 September 1945. Thus ended the war in Asia, cementing the total victory of the Allies.</p>
<p>World War II altered the political alignment and social structure of the world. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (UN) was established to foster international co-operation and prevent future conflicts. The victorious <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">great powers</a>—China, France, the Soviet Union, the United Kingdom, and the United States—became the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council" title="Permanent members of the United Nations Security Council">permanent members</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_UN_Security_Council_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_UN_Security_Council-9">[7]</a></sup> The Soviet Union and the United States emerged as rival <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">superpowers</a>, setting the stage for the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, which lasted for the next 46 years. Meanwhile, the influence of European great powers waned, while the <a href="/wiki/Decolonisation_of_Africa" title="Decolonisation of Africa">decolonisation of Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Decolonisation_of_Asia" title="Decolonisation of Asia">Asia</a> began. Most countries whose industries had been damaged moved towards <a href="/wiki/Post%E2%80%93World_War_II_economic_expansion" title="Post–World War II economic expansion">economic recovery</a>. Political integration, especially <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">in Europe</a>, emerged as an effort to end pre-war enmities and to create a common identity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[8]</a></sup></p>

<p>The start of the war in Europe is generally held to be 1 September 1939,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeinberg20056_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeinberg20056-11">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup> beginning with the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">German invasion of Poland</a>; Britain and France declared war on Germany two days later. The dates for the beginning of war in the Pacific include the start of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a> on 7 July 1937,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEF.C3.B6rsterGessler200564_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEF.C3.B6rsterGessler200564-14">[12]</a></sup> or even the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Manchuria" title="Japanese invasion of Manchuria">Japanese invasion of Manchuria</a> on 19 September 1931.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Others follow the British historian <a href="/wiki/A._J._P._Taylor" title="A. J. P. Taylor">A. J. P. Taylor</a>, who held that the Sino-Japanese War and war in Europe and its colonies occurred simultaneously and the two wars merged in 1941. This article uses the conventional dating. Other starting dates sometimes used for World War II include the <a href="/wiki/Second_Italo-Ethiopian_War" title="Second Italo-Ethiopian War">Italian invasion of Abyssinia</a> on 3 October 1935.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[15]</a></sup> The British historian <a href="/wiki/Antony_Beevor" title="Antony Beevor">Antony Beevor</a> views the beginning of World War II as the <a href="/wiki/Battles_of_Khalkhin_Gol" title="Battles of Khalkhin Gol">Battles of Khalkhin Gol</a> fought between Japan and the forces of <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> and the Soviet Union from May to September 1939.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeevor201210_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor201210-18">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>The exact date of the war's end is also not universally agreed upon. It was generally accepted at the time that the war ended with the <a href="/wiki/Armistice" title="Armistice">armistice</a> of 14 August 1945 (<a href="/wiki/Victory_over_Japan_Day" title="Victory over Japan Day">V-J Day</a>), rather than the formal surrender of Japan (2 September 1945). A <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_San_Francisco" title="Treaty of San Francisco">peace treaty with Japan</a> was signed in 1951.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasaya19904_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasaya19904-19">[17]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Final_Settlement_with_Respect_to_Germany" title="Treaty on the Final Settlement with Respect to Germany">treaty regarding Germany's future</a> allowed the <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">reunification of East and West Germany</a> to take place in 1990 and resolved other post-World War II issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Causes_of_World_War_II" title="Causes of World War II">Causes of World War II</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> had radically altered the <a href="/wiki/Geopolitics" title="Geopolitics">political</a> European map, with the defeat of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a>—including <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bulgaria" title="Kingdom of Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>—and the 1917 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolshevik" title="Bolshevik">Bolshevik</a> <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">seizure of power</a> in <a href="/wiki/Russian_Republic" title="Russian Republic">Russia</a>, which eventually led to the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. Meanwhile, the victorious <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allies of World War I</a>, such as France, Belgium, Italy, Romania and Greece gained territory, and new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nation-states" title="Nation-states">nation-states</a> were created out of the collapse of Austria-Hungary and the Ottoman and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empires</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-09042,_Genf,_V%C3%B6lkerbund,_Sitzungssaal.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="528" data-file-width="795" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-09042%2C_Genf%2C_V%C3%B6lkerbund%2C_Sitzungssaal.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-09042%2C_Genf%2C_V%C3%B6lkerbund%2C_Sitzungssaal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-09042%2C_Genf%2C_V%C3%B6lkerbund%2C_Sitzungssaal.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-09042%2C_Genf%2C_V%C3%B6lkerbund%2C_Sitzungssaal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-09042%2C_Genf%2C_V%C3%B6lkerbund%2C_Sitzungssaal.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-09042%2C_Genf%2C_V%C3%B6lkerbund%2C_Sitzungssaal.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-09042,_Genf,_V%C3%B6lkerbund,_Sitzungssaal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> assembly, held in <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, 1930</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>To prevent a future world war, the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> was created during the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference,_1919" title="Paris Peace Conference, 1919">1919 Paris Peace Conference</a>. The organisation's primary goals were to prevent armed conflict through <a href="/wiki/Collective_security" title="Collective security">collective security</a>, military and <a href="/wiki/Washington_Naval_Treaty" title="Washington Naval Treaty">naval disarmament</a>, and settling international disputes through peaceful negotiations and arbitration.</p>
<p>Despite strong <a href="/wiki/Pacifism" title="Pacifism">pacifist</a> sentiment <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_I" title="Aftermath of World War I">after World War I</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIngram2006.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DbREQibN9i-sC.26pg.3DPA76_76.E2.80.938.5D_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIngram2006.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DbREQibN9i-sC.26pg.3DPA76_76.E2.80.938.5D-21">[19]</a></sup> its aftermath still caused <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irredentist" title="Irredentist">irredentist</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revanchist" title="Revanchist">revanchist</a> <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalism</a> in several European states. These sentiments were especially marked in Germany because of the significant territorial, colonial, and financial losses incurred by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a>. Under the treaty, Germany lost around 13 per cent of its home territory and all of <a href="/wiki/German_colonial_empire" title="German colonial empire">its overseas possessions</a>, while German annexation of other states was prohibited, <a href="/wiki/World_War_I_reparations" title="World War I reparations">reparations</a> were imposed, and limits were placed on the size and capability of the country's <a href="/wiki/Reichswehr" title="Reichswehr">armed forces</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKantowicz1999149_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKantowicz1999149-22">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>The German Empire was dissolved in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Revolution_of_1918%E2%80%931919" title="German Revolution of 1918–1919">German Revolution of 1918–1919</a>, and a democratic government, later known as the <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">Weimar Republic</a>, was created. The interwar period saw strife between supporters of the new republic and hardline opponents on both the <a href="/wiki/Right-wing_politics" title="Right-wing politics">right</a> and <a href="/wiki/Left-wing_politics" title="Left-wing politics">left</a>. Italy, as an Entente ally, had made some post-war territorial gains; however, Italian nationalists were angered that the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_London_(1915)" title="Treaty of London (1915)">promises made</a> by Britain and France to secure Italian entrance into the war were not fulfilled in the peace settlement. From 1922 to 1925, the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Fascism" title="Italian Fascism">Fascist</a> movement led by <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a> seized power in Italy with a nationalist, <a href="/wiki/Totalitarianism" title="Totalitarianism">totalitarian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Class_collaboration" title="Class collaboration">class collaborationist</a> agenda that abolished representative democracy, repressed socialist, left-wing and liberal forces, and pursued an aggressive expansionist foreign policy aimed at making Italy a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_power" title="World power">world power</a>, promising the creation of a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Roman_Empire" title="New Roman Empire">New Roman Empire</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShaw200035_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShaw200035-23">[21]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10541,_Weimar,_Aufmarsch_der_Nationalsozialisten.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="544" data-file-width="800" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10541%2C_Weimar%2C_Aufmarsch_der_Nationalsozialisten.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10541%2C_Weimar%2C_Aufmarsch_der_Nationalsozialisten.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10541%2C_Weimar%2C_Aufmarsch_der_Nationalsozialisten.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10541%2C_Weimar%2C_Aufmarsch_der_Nationalsozialisten.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10541%2C_Weimar%2C_Aufmarsch_der_Nationalsozialisten.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10541%2C_Weimar%2C_Aufmarsch_der_Nationalsozialisten.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10541,_Weimar,_Aufmarsch_der_Nationalsozialisten.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> at a German <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Socialist" title="National Socialist">National Socialist</a> political rally in <a href="/wiki/Weimar" title="Weimar">Weimar</a>, October 1930</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Adolf Hitler, after an <a href="/wiki/Beer_Hall_Putsch" title="Beer Hall Putsch">unsuccessful attempt to overthrow the German government</a> in 1923, eventually became the <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler%27s_rise_to_power" title="Adolf Hitler's rise to power">Chancellor of Germany in 1933</a>. He abolished democracy, espousing a <a href="/wiki/New_Order_(Nazism)" title="New Order (Nazism)">radical, racially motivated revision of the world order</a>, and soon began a massive <a href="/wiki/German_re-armament" title="German re-armament">rearmament campaign</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrody19994_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrody19994-24">[22]</a></sup> Meanwhile, France, to secure its alliance, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franco-Italian_Agreement" title="Franco-Italian Agreement">allowed Italy a free hand in Ethiopia</a>, which Italy desired as a colonial possession. The situation was aggravated in early 1935 when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saar_(League_of_Nations)" title="Saar (League of Nations)">Territory of the Saar Basin</a> was legally reunited with Germany and Hitler repudiated the Treaty of Versailles, accelerated his rearmament programme, and introduced <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscription</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZalampas198962_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZalampas198962-25">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>To contain Germany, the United Kingdom, France and Italy formed the <a href="/wiki/Stresa_Front" title="Stresa Front">Stresa Front</a> in April 1935; however, that June, the United Kingdom made an <a href="/wiki/Anglo-German_Naval_Agreement" title="Anglo-German Naval Agreement">independent naval agreement</a> with Germany, easing prior restrictions. The Soviet Union, concerned by <a href="/wiki/Drang_nach_Osten" title="Drang nach Osten">Germany's goals of capturing vast areas of Eastern Europe</a>, drafted a treaty of mutual assistance with France. Before taking effect though, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franco-Soviet_pact" title="Franco-Soviet pact">Franco-Soviet pact</a> was required to go through the bureaucracy of the League of Nations, which rendered it essentially toothless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup> The United States, concerned with events in Europe and Asia, passed the <a href="/wiki/Neutrality_Acts_of_1930s" title="Neutrality Acts of 1930s">Neutrality Act</a> in August of the same year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmitz2000124_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitz2000124-27">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hitler defied the Versailles and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Locarno_treaties" title="Locarno treaties">Locarno treaties</a> by <a href="/wiki/Remilitarization_of_the_Rhineland" title="Remilitarization of the Rhineland">remilitarising</a> the <a href="/wiki/Rhineland" title="Rhineland">Rhineland</a> in March 1936, encountering little opposition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdamthwaite199252_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdamthwaite199252-28">[26]</a></sup> In October 1936, Germany and Italy formed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rome%E2%80%93Berlin_Axis" title="Rome–Berlin Axis">Rome–Berlin Axis</a>. A month later, Germany and Japan signed the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Comintern_Pact" title="Anti-Comintern Pact">Anti-Comintern Pact</a>, which Italy would join in the following year.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a> (KMT) party in China launched a <a href="/wiki/Northern_Expedition" title="Northern Expedition">unification campaign</a> against <a href="/wiki/Warlord_Era" title="Warlord Era">regional warlords</a> and nominally unified China in the mid-1920s, but was soon embroiled in a <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">civil war</a> against its former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party" title="Chinese Communist Party">Chinese Communist Party</a> allies<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPreston1998104_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPreston1998104-29">[27]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Plains_War" title="Central Plains War">new regional warlords</a>. In 1931, an <a href="/wiki/Statism_in_Sh%C5%8Dwa_Japan" title="Statism in Shōwa Japan">increasingly militaristic</a> <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a>, which had long sought influence in China<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMyersPeattie1987458_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMyersPeattie1987458-30">[28]</a></sup> as the first step of what its government saw as the country's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hakko_ichiu" title="Hakko ichiu">right to rule Asia</a>, used the <a href="/wiki/Mukden_Incident" title="Mukden Incident">Mukden Incident</a> as a pretext to <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Manchuria" title="Japanese invasion of Manchuria">launch an invasion of Manchuria</a> and establish the <a href="/wiki/Puppet_state" title="Puppet state">puppet state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Manchukuo" title="Manchukuo">Manchukuo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmithSteadman200428_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmithSteadman200428-31">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Too weak to resist Japan, China appealed to the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> for help. Japan withdrew from the League of Nations after being <a href="/wiki/Lytton_Report" title="Lytton Report">condemned</a> for its incursion into Manchuria. The two nations then fought several battles, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/28_January_Incident" title="28 January Incident">Shanghai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Rehe" title="Battle of Rehe">Rehe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Defense_of_the_Great_Wall" title="Defense of the Great Wall">Hebei</a>, until the <a href="/wiki/Tanggu_Truce" title="Tanggu Truce">Tanggu Truce</a> was signed in 1933. Thereafter, Chinese volunteer forces continued the resistance to Japanese aggression in <a href="/wiki/Pacification_of_Manchukuo" title="Pacification of Manchukuo">Manchuria</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Actions_in_Inner_Mongolia_(1933%E2%80%931936)" title="Actions in Inner Mongolia (1933–1936)">Chahar and Suiyuan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup> After the 1936 <a href="/wiki/Xi%27an_Incident" title="Xi'an Incident">Xi'an Incident</a>, the Kuomintang and communist forces agreed on a ceasefire to present a <a href="/wiki/Second_United_Front" title="Second United Front">united front</a> to oppose Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBusky200210_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBusky200210-33">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-war_events">Pre-war events</span></h2>
<h3><span id="Italian_invasion_of_Ethiopia_(1935)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Italian_invasion_of_Ethiopia_.281935.29">Italian invasion of Ethiopia (1935)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Second_Italo-Ethiopian_War" title="Second Italo-Ethiopian War">Second Italo-Ethiopian War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Soldatietiopia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1261" data-file-width="2000" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Soldatietiopia.jpg/220px-Soldatietiopia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Soldatietiopia.jpg/330px-Soldatietiopia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Soldatietiopia.jpg/440px-Soldatietiopia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Soldatietiopia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Italian soldiers recruited in 1935, on their way to fight the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_Italo-Abyssinian_War" title="Second Italo-Abyssinian War">Second Italo-Abyssinian War</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Second Italo–Abyssinian War was a brief <a href="/wiki/Colonial_war" title="Colonial war">colonial war</a> that began in October 1935 and ended in May 1936. The war began with the invasion of the <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Empire" title="Ethiopian Empire">Ethiopian Empire</a> (also known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Names_of_Ethiopia" title="Names of Ethiopia">Abyssinia</a>) by the armed forces of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Kingdom of Italy</a> (<i>Regno d'Italia</i>), which was launched from <a href="/wiki/Italian_Somaliland" title="Italian Somaliland">Italian Somaliland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_Eritrea" title="Italian Eritrea">Eritrea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup> The war resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Military_occupation" title="Military occupation">military occupation</a> of Ethiopia and its <a href="/wiki/Annexation" title="Annexation">annexation</a> into the newly created colony of <a href="/wiki/Italian_East_Africa" title="Italian East Africa">Italian East Africa</a> (<i>Africa Orientale Italiana</i>, or AOI); in addition it exposed the weakness of the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> as a force to preserve peace. Both Italy and Ethiopia were member nations, but the League did nothing when the former clearly violated the League's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Article_X_of_the_Covenant_of_the_League_of_Nations" title="Article X of the Covenant of the League of Nations">Article X</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker1971131.E2.80.932_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker1971131.E2.80.932-35">[33]</a></sup> Germany was the only major European nation to support the invasion. Italy subsequently dropped its objections to Germany's goal of absorbing <a href="/wiki/Federal_State_of_Austria" title="Federal State of Austria">Austria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKitson2001231_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKitson2001231-36">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Spanish_Civil_War_(1936–39)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_Civil_War_.281936.E2.80.9339.29">Spanish Civil War (1936–39)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H25224,_Guernica,_Ruinen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="584" data-file-width="798" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H25224%2C_Guernica%2C_Ruinen.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H25224%2C_Guernica%2C_Ruinen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H25224%2C_Guernica%2C_Ruinen.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H25224%2C_Guernica%2C_Ruinen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H25224%2C_Guernica%2C_Ruinen.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H25224%2C_Guernica%2C_Ruinen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H25224,_Guernica,_Ruinen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Guernica" title="Bombing of Guernica">bombing of Guernica</a> in 1937, during the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>, sparked Europe-wide fears that the next war would be based on bombing of cities with very high civilian casualties</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>When civil war broke out in Spain, Hitler and Mussolini lent military support to the <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_faction_(Spanish_Civil_War)" title="Nationalist faction (Spanish Civil War)">Nationalist rebels</a>, led by General <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a>. The Soviet Union supported the existing government, the <a href="/wiki/Second_Spanish_Republic" title="Second Spanish Republic">Spanish Republic</a>. Over 30,000 foreign volunteers, known as the <a href="/wiki/International_Brigades" title="International Brigades">International Brigades</a>, also fought against the Nationalists. Both Germany and the USSR used this <a href="/wiki/Proxy_war" title="Proxy war">proxy war</a> as an opportunity to test in combat their most advanced weapons and tactics. The Nationalists won the civil war in April 1939; Franco, now dictator, remained officially neutral during Second World War but generally favoured the Axis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPayne2008271_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPayne2008271-37">[35]</a></sup> His greatest collaboration with Germany was the sending of <a href="/wiki/Blue_Division" title="Blue Division">volunteers</a> to fight on the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPayne2008146_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPayne2008146-38">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Japanese_invasion_of_China_(1937)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Japanese_invasion_of_China_.281937.29">Japanese invasion of China (1937)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shanghai1937IJA_ruins.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="315" data-file-width="500" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Shanghai1937IJA_ruins.jpg/220px-Shanghai1937IJA_ruins.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Shanghai1937IJA_ruins.jpg/330px-Shanghai1937IJA_ruins.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Shanghai1937IJA_ruins.jpg/440px-Shanghai1937IJA_ruins.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shanghai1937IJA_ruins.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Imperial_Army" title="Japanese Imperial Army">Japanese Imperial Army</a> soldiers during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Shanghai" title="Battle of Shanghai">Battle of Shanghai</a>, 1937</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In July 1937, Japan captured the former Chinese imperial capital of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peking" title="Peking">Peking</a> after instigating the <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo_Bridge_Incident" title="Marco Polo Bridge Incident">Marco Polo Bridge Incident</a>, which culminated in the Japanese campaign to invade all of China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEastman1986547.E2.80.9351_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEastman1986547.E2.80.9351-39">[37]</a></sup> The Soviets quickly signed a <a href="/wiki/Sino-Soviet_Non-Aggression_Pact" title="Sino-Soviet Non-Aggression Pact">non-aggression pact with China</a> to lend <a href="/wiki/Materiel" title="Materiel">materiel</a> support, effectively ending China's prior <a href="/wiki/Sino-German_cooperation_1926%E2%80%931941" title="Sino-German cooperation 1926–1941">co-operation with Germany</a>. From September to November, the Japanese attacked <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Taiyuan" title="Battle of Taiyuan">Taiyuan</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guo_1971_221_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guo_1971_221-40">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hsu_.26_Chang_1971_221_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hsu_.26_Chang_1971_221-41">[39]</a></sup> as well as engaging the <a href="/wiki/National_Revolutionary_Army" title="National Revolutionary Army">Kuomintang Army</a> <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Xinkou" title="Battle of Xinkou">around Xinkou</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guo_1971_221_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guo_1971_221-40">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hsu_.26_Chang_1971_221_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hsu_.26_Chang_1971_221-41">[39]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">Communist forces</a> <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pingxingguan" title="Battle of Pingxingguan">in Pingxingguan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tucker2009_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker2009-42">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yang_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-yang-43">[41]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Generalissimo" title="Generalissimo">Generalissimo</a> <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a> deployed his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German-trained_divisions_in_the_National_Revolutionary_Army" title="German-trained divisions in the National Revolutionary Army">best army</a> to <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Shanghai" title="Battle of Shanghai">defend Shanghai</a>, but, after three months of fighting, Shanghai fell. The Japanese continued to push the Chinese forces back, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nanking" title="Battle of Nanking">capturing the capital Nanking</a> in December 1937. After the fall of Nanking, tens of thousands if not hundreds of thousands of Chinese civilians and disarmed combatants were <a href="/wiki/Nanking_Massacre" title="Nanking Massacre">murdered by the Japanese</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tot_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-tot-45">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 1938, Nationalist Chinese forces won their <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Taierzhuang" title="Battle of Taierzhuang">first major victory at Taierzhuang</a> but then the city of <a href="/wiki/Xuzhou" title="Xuzhou">Xuzhou</a> <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Xuzhou" title="Battle of Xuzhou">was taken by Japanese</a> in May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHsuChang1971221.E2.80.93230_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHsuChang1971221.E2.80.93230-46">[44]</a></sup> In June 1938, Chinese forces stalled the Japanese advance by <a href="/wiki/1938_Yellow_River_flood" title="1938 Yellow River flood">flooding the Yellow River</a>; this manoeuvre bought time for the Chinese to prepare their defences at <a href="/wiki/Wuhan" title="Wuhan">Wuhan</a>, but the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wuhan" title="Battle of Wuhan">city was taken</a> by October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEastman1986566_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEastman1986566-47">[45]</a></sup> Japanese military victories did not bring about the collapse of Chinese resistance that Japan had hoped to achieve; instead the Chinese government relocated inland to <a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">Chongqing</a> and continued the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaylor2009150.E2.80.932_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor2009150.E2.80.932-48">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESella1983651.E2.80.9387_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESella1983651.E2.80.9387-49">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Soviet–Japanese_border_conflicts"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet.E2.80.93Japanese_border_conflicts">Soviet–Japanese border conflicts</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Lake_Khasan-Red_Army_gunners_in_the_interval.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="553" data-file-width="780" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Battle_of_Lake_Khasan-Red_Army_gunners_in_the_interval.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Lake_Khasan-Red_Army_gunners_in_the_interval.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Battle_of_Lake_Khasan-Red_Army_gunners_in_the_interval.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Lake_Khasan-Red_Army_gunners_in_the_interval.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Battle_of_Lake_Khasan-Red_Army_gunners_in_the_interval.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Lake_Khasan-Red_Army_gunners_in_the_interval.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Lake_Khasan-Red_Army_gunners_in_the_interval.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> artillery unit during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lake_Khasan" title="Battle of Lake Khasan">Battle of Lake Khasan</a>, 1938</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Japanese_border_conflicts" title="Soviet–Japanese border conflicts">Soviet–Japanese border conflicts</a></div>
<p>In the mid-to-late 1930s, Japanese forces in <a href="/wiki/Manchukuo" title="Manchukuo">Manchukuo</a> had sporadic border clashes with the Soviet Union and the <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_People%27s_Republic" title="Mongolian People's Republic">Mongolian People's Republic</a>. The Japanese doctrine of <a href="/wiki/Hokushin-ron" title="Hokushin-ron">Hokushin-ron</a>, which emphasised Japan's expansion northward, was favoured by the Imperial Army during this time. With the Japanese defeat at <a href="/wiki/Battles_of_Khalkhin_Gol" title="Battles of Khalkhin Gol">Khalkin Gol</a> in 1939, the ongoing Second Sino-Japanese War<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012342_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012342-50">[48]</a></sup> and ally Nazi Germany pursuing neutrality with the Soviets, this policy would prove difficult to maintain. Japan and the Soviet Union eventually signed a <a href="/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Japanese_Neutrality_Pact" title="Soviet–Japanese Neutrality Pact">Neutrality Pact</a> in April 1941, and Japan adopted the doctrine of <a href="/wiki/Nanshin-ron" title="Nanshin-ron">Nanshin-ron</a>, promoted by the Navy, which took its focus southward, eventually leading to its war with the United States and the Western Allies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_occupations_and_agreements">European occupations and agreements</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Anschluss" title="Anschluss">Anschluss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Appeasement" title="Appeasement">Appeasement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Munich_Agreement" title="Munich Agreement">Munich Agreement</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Czechoslovakia" title="German occupation of Czechoslovakia">German occupation of Czechoslovakia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact">Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R69173,_M%C3%BCnchener_Abkommen,_Staatschefs.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="548" data-file-width="800" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R69173%2C_M%C3%BCnchener_Abkommen%2C_Staatschefs.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R69173%2C_M%C3%BCnchener_Abkommen%2C_Staatschefs.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R69173%2C_M%C3%BCnchener_Abkommen%2C_Staatschefs.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R69173%2C_M%C3%BCnchener_Abkommen%2C_Staatschefs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R69173%2C_M%C3%BCnchener_Abkommen%2C_Staatschefs.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R69173%2C_M%C3%BCnchener_Abkommen%2C_Staatschefs.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R69173,_M%C3%BCnchener_Abkommen,_Staatschefs.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Neville_Chamberlain" title="Neville Chamberlain">Chamberlain</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%89douard_Daladier" title="Édouard Daladier">Daladier</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hitler" title="Hitler">Hitler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Mussolini</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Galeazzo_Ciano" title="Galeazzo Ciano">Ciano</a> pictured just before signing the <a href="/wiki/Munich_Agreement" title="Munich Agreement">Munich Agreement</a>, 29 September 1938</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Europe, Germany and Italy were becoming more aggressive. In March 1938, Germany <a href="/wiki/Anschluss" title="Anschluss">annexed Austria</a>, again provoking <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Appeasement_of_Hitler" title="Appeasement of Hitler">little response</a> from other European powers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollierPedley2000144_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollierPedley2000144-53">[51]</a></sup> Encouraged, Hitler began pressing German claims on the <a href="/wiki/Sudetenland" title="Sudetenland">Sudetenland</a>, an area of <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> with a predominantly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_German" title="Ethnic German">ethnic German</a> population; and soon Britain and France followed the counsel of British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Neville_Chamberlain" title="Neville Chamberlain">Neville Chamberlain</a> and conceded this territory to Germany in the <a href="/wiki/Munich_Agreement" title="Munich Agreement">Munich Agreement</a>, which was made against the wishes of the Czechoslovak government, in exchange for a promise of no further territorial demands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2001121.E2.80.932_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2001121.E2.80.932-54">[52]</a></sup> Soon afterwards, Germany and Italy forced Czechoslovakia to <a href="/wiki/First_Vienna_Award" title="First Vienna Award">cede additional territory</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> and Poland annexed Czechoslovakia's <a href="/wiki/Zaolzie" title="Zaolzie">Zaolzie</a> region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2001157_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2001157-55">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although all of Germany's stated demands had been satisfied by the agreement, privately Hitler was furious that British interference had prevented him from seizing all of Czechoslovakia in one operation. In subsequent speeches Hitler attacked British and Jewish "war-mongers" and in January 1939 <a href="/wiki/Plan_Z" title="Plan Z">secretly ordered a major build-up of the German navy</a> to challenge British naval supremacy. In March 1939, <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Czechoslovakia" title="German occupation of Czechoslovakia">Germany invaded the remainder of Czechoslovakia</a> and subsequently split it into the German <a href="/wiki/Protectorate_of_Bohemia_and_Moravia" title="Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia">Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia</a> and a pro-German <a href="/wiki/Client_state" title="Client state">client state</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Republic_(1939%E2%80%931945)" title="Slovak Republic (1939–1945)">Slovak Republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies2006pp._143.E2.80.934_.282008_ed..29_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2006pp._143.E2.80.934_.282008_ed..29-56">[54]</a></sup> Hitler also delivered <a href="/wiki/1939_German_ultimatum_to_Lithuania" title="1939 German ultimatum to Lithuania">an ultimatum</a> to Lithuania, forcing the concession of the <a href="/wiki/Klaip%C4%97da_Region" title="Klaipėda Region">Klaipėda Region</a>.</p>
<p>Greatly alarmed and with Hitler making further demands on the <a href="/wiki/Free_City_of_Danzig" title="Free City of Danzig">Free City of Danzig</a>, Britain and France <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Polish_military_alliance#British_Guarantee_to_Poland" title="Anglo-Polish military alliance">guaranteed their support for Polish independence</a>; when <a href="/wiki/Italian_invasion_of_Albania" title="Italian invasion of Albania">Italy conquered Albania</a> in April 1939, the same guarantee was extended to Romania and <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELoweMarzari2002330_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELoweMarzari2002330-57">[55]</a></sup> Shortly after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franco-Polish_Military_Alliance" title="Franco-Polish Military Alliance">Franco</a>-British pledge to Poland, Germany and Italy formalised their own alliance with the <a href="/wiki/Pact_of_Steel" title="Pact of Steel">Pact of Steel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001234_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001234-58">[56]</a></sup> Hitler accused Britain and Poland of trying to "encircle" Germany and renounced the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-German_Naval_Agreement" title="Anglo-German Naval Agreement">Anglo-German Naval Agreement</a> and the <a href="/wiki/German%E2%80%93Polish_Non-Aggression_Pact" title="German–Polish Non-Aggression Pact">German–Polish Non-Aggression Pact</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27337,_Moskau,_Stalin_und_Ribbentrop_im_Kreml.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="545" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27337%2C_Moskau%2C_Stalin_und_Ribbentrop_im_Kreml.jpg/170px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27337%2C_Moskau%2C_Stalin_und_Ribbentrop_im_Kreml.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27337%2C_Moskau%2C_Stalin_und_Ribbentrop_im_Kreml.jpg/255px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27337%2C_Moskau%2C_Stalin_und_Ribbentrop_im_Kreml.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27337%2C_Moskau%2C_Stalin_und_Ribbentrop_im_Kreml.jpg/340px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27337%2C_Moskau%2C_Stalin_und_Ribbentrop_im_Kreml.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27337,_Moskau,_Stalin_und_Ribbentrop_im_Kreml.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
German Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Joachim_von_Ribbentrop" title="Joachim von Ribbentrop">Joachim von Ribbentrop</a> (right) and the Soviet leader <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>, after signing the <a href="/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact">Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact</a>, 23 August 1939</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In August 1939, Germany and the Soviet Union signed the <a href="/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact">Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShore2003108_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShore2003108-59">[57]</a></sup> a non-aggression treaty with a secret protocol. The parties gave each other rights to "spheres of influence" (western <a href="/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic" title="Second Polish Republic">Poland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> for Germany; <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_Poland_annexed_by_the_Soviet_Union" title="Territories of Poland annexed by the Soviet Union">eastern Poland</a>, Finland, <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, Latvia and <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a> for the USSR). It also raised the question of continuing Polish independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001608_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001608-60">[58]</a></sup> The agreement was crucial to Hitler because it assured that Germany would not have to face the prospect of a two-front war, as it had in World War I, after it defeated Poland.</p>
<p>The situation reached a general crisis in late August as German troops continued to mobilise against the Polish border. In a private meeting with the Italian foreign minister, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Count_Ciano" title="Count Ciano">Count Ciano</a>, Hitler asserted that Poland was a "doubtful neutral" that needed to either yield to his demands or be "liquidated" to prevent it from drawing off German troops in the future "unavoidable" war with the Western democracies. He did not believe Britain or France would intervene in the conflict.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup> On 23 August Hitler ordered the attack to proceed on 26 August, but upon hearing that Britain had concluded a formal mutual assistance pact with Poland and that Italy would maintain neutrality, he decided to delay it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>In response to British requests for direct negotiations to avoid war, Germany made demands on Poland, which only served as a pretext to worsen relations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ww2db_com_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-ww2db_com-63">[61]</a></sup> On 29 August, Hitler demanded that a Polish <a href="/wiki/Plenipotentiary" title="Plenipotentiary">plenipotentiary</a> immediately travel to Berlin to negotiate the handover of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danzig" title="Danzig">Danzig</a>, and to allow a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plebiscite" title="Plebiscite">plebiscite</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Corridor" title="Polish Corridor">Polish Corridor</a> in which the German minority would vote on secession.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ww2db_com_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-ww2db_com-63">[61]</a></sup> The Poles refused to comply with the German demands and on the night of 30–31 August in a violent meeting with the British ambassador <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neville_Henderson" title="Neville Henderson">Neville Henderson</a>, Ribbentrop declared that Germany considered its claims rejected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibiblio1939_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-ibiblio1939-64">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Course_of_the_war">Course of the war</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_history_of_World_War_II" title="Diplomatic history of World War II">Diplomatic history of World War II</a></div>
<h3><span id="War_breaks_out_in_Europe_(1939–40)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="War_breaks_out_in_Europe_.281939.E2.80.9340.29">War breaks out in Europe (1939–40)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">Invasion of Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoney_War" title="Phoney War">Phoney War</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Poland_(1939%E2%80%9345)" title="Occupation of Poland (1939–45)">Occupation of Poland (1939–45)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nazi_crimes_against_the_Polish_nation" title="Nazi crimes against the Polish nation">Nazi crimes against the Polish nation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Poland" title="Soviet invasion of Poland">Soviet invasion of Poland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_repressions_of_Polish_citizens_(1939%E2%80%931946)" title="Soviet repressions of Polish citizens (1939–1946)">Soviet repressions of Polish citizens (1939–1946)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Germans_at_Polish_Border_(1939-09-01).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1033" data-file-width="1500" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Germans_at_Polish_Border_%281939-09-01%29.jpg/220px-Germans_at_Polish_Border_%281939-09-01%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Germans_at_Polish_Border_%281939-09-01%29.jpg/330px-Germans_at_Polish_Border_%281939-09-01%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Germans_at_Polish_Border_%281939-09-01%29.jpg/440px-Germans_at_Polish_Border_%281939-09-01%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Germans_at_Polish_Border_(1939-09-01).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Soldiers of the German <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a> tearing down the border crossing between <a href="/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic" title="Second Polish Republic">Poland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Free_City_of_Danzig" title="Free City of Danzig">Free City of Danzig</a>, 1 September 1939</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 1 September 1939, Germany <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">invaded Poland</a> under the false pretext that the Poles had carried out a series of <a href="/wiki/Gleiwitz_incident" title="Gleiwitz incident">sabotage operations</a> against German targets near the border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans20081.E2.80.932_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans20081.E2.80.932-65">[63]</a></sup> Two days later, on 3 September, after a British ultimatum to Germany to cease military operations was ignored, Britain and France, followed by the fully independent <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">Dominions</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson200658_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson200658-66">[64]</a></sup> of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">British Commonwealth</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeinberg200564.E2.80.935_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeinberg200564.E2.80.935-67">[65]</a></sup>—<a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> (3 September), <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> (10 September), <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> (3 September), and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> (6 September)—declared war on Germany. However, initially the alliance provided <a href="/wiki/Phoney_War" title="Phoney War">limited direct military support</a> to Poland, consisting of a <a href="/wiki/Saar_Offensive" title="Saar Offensive">cautious, half-hearted French probe into the Saarland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Keegan_1997_35_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Keegan_1997_35-68">[66]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Western Allies</a> also began a <a href="/wiki/Blockade_of_Germany_(1939%E2%80%9345)" title="Blockade of Germany (1939–45)">naval blockade of Germany</a>, which aimed to damage the country's economy and war effort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> Germany responded by ordering <a href="/wiki/Submarine_warfare#World_War_II" title="Submarine warfare">U-boat warfare</a> against Allied merchant and warships, which was to later escalate into the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Atlantic" title="Battle of the Atlantic">Battle of the Atlantic</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1976-071-36,_Polen,_an_der_Brahe,_deutsche_Panzer.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="796" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1976-071-36%2C_Polen%2C_an_der_Brahe%2C_deutsche_Panzer.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1976-071-36%2C_Polen%2C_an_der_Brahe%2C_deutsche_Panzer.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1976-071-36%2C_Polen%2C_an_der_Brahe%2C_deutsche_Panzer.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1976-071-36%2C_Polen%2C_an_der_Brahe%2C_deutsche_Panzer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1976-071-36%2C_Polen%2C_an_der_Brahe%2C_deutsche_Panzer.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1976-071-36%2C_Polen%2C_an_der_Brahe%2C_deutsche_Panzer.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1976-071-36,_Polen,_an_der_Brahe,_deutsche_Panzer.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
German tanks near the city of <a href="/wiki/Bydgoszcz" title="Bydgoszcz">Bydgoszcz</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">Invasion of Poland</a> September, 1939</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 17 September 1939, after signing a <a href="/wiki/Battles_of_Khalkhin_Gol" title="Battles of Khalkhin Gol">cease-fire with Japan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Poland" title="Soviet invasion of Poland">Soviets invaded Poland</a> from the east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZaloga200280.2C_83_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZaloga200280.2C_83-70">[68]</a></sup> The Polish army was defeated and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Warsaw_(1939)" title="Battle of Warsaw (1939)">Warsaw surrendered</a> to the Germans on 27 September with final pockets of resistance surrendering on 6 October. Poland's territory was divided between <a href="/wiki/Polish_areas_annexed_by_Nazi_Germany" title="Polish areas annexed by Nazi Germany">Germany</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_Poland_annexed_by_the_Soviet_Union" title="Territories of Poland annexed by the Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territorial_changes_of_Poland#World_War_II" title="Territorial changes of Poland">Lithuania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovak_invasion_of_Poland_(1939)" title="Slovak invasion of Poland (1939)">Slovakia</a> also receiving small shares. After the defeat of Poland's armed forces, the Polish resistance established an <a href="/wiki/Polish_Underground_State" title="Polish Underground State">Underground State</a> and a partisan <a href="/wiki/Home_Army" title="Home Army">Home Army</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHempel200524_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHempel200524-71">[69]</a></sup> About 100,000 Polish military personnel were <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Bridgehead" title="Romanian Bridgehead">evacuated to Romania</a> and the Baltic countries; many of these soldiers later fought against the Germans in other theatres of the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZaloga200288.E2.80.939_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZaloga200288.E2.80.939-72">[70]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Biuro_Szyfr%C3%B3w" title="Biuro Szyfrów">Poland's Enigma codebreakers</a> were also evacuated to France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBudiansky2001120.E2.80.931_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBudiansky2001120.E2.80.931-73">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 6 October, Hitler made a public peace overture to Britain and France, but said that the future of Poland was to be determined exclusively by Germany and the Soviet Union. Chamberlain rejected this on 12 October, saying "Past experience has shown that no reliance can be placed upon the promises of the present German Government."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibiblio1939_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-ibiblio1939-64">[62]</a></sup> After this rejection Hitler ordered an immediate offensive against France,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup> but bad weather forced repeated postponements until the spring of 1940.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELiddell_Hart197739.E2.80.9340_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELiddell_Hart197739.E2.80.9340-75">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1990pp._563.E2.80.934.2C_566.2C_568.E2.80.939.2C_574.E2.80.935_.281983_ed..29_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1990pp._563.E2.80.934.2C_566.2C_568.E2.80.939.2C_574.E2.80.935_.281983_ed..29-76">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spotkanie_Sojusznik%C3%B3w.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="564" data-file-width="816" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Spotkanie_Sojusznik%C3%B3w.jpg/220px-Spotkanie_Sojusznik%C3%B3w.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Spotkanie_Sojusznik%C3%B3w.jpg/330px-Spotkanie_Sojusznik%C3%B3w.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Spotkanie_Sojusznik%C3%B3w.jpg/440px-Spotkanie_Sojusznik%C3%B3w.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spotkanie_Sojusznik%C3%B3w.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
German and Soviet army officers pictured shaking hands—after <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> annexed new territories in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>, 1939</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After signing the <a href="/wiki/German%E2%80%93Soviet_Frontier_Treaty" title="German–Soviet Frontier Treaty">German–Soviet Treaty of Friendship, Cooperation and Demarcation</a>, the Soviet Union forced the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic countries</a>—Estonia, Latvia and Lithuania—to allow it <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Baltic_states#Ultimatums_to_Estonia.2C_Latvia.2C_Lithuania" title="Occupation of Baltic states">to station Soviet troops in their countries under pacts of "mutual assistance"</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmithPabriksPursLane200224_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmithPabriksPursLane200224-78">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBilinsky19999_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBilinsky19999-79">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMurrayMillett200155.E2.80.936_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMurrayMillett200155.E2.80.936-80">[78]</a></sup> Finland rejected territorial demands, prompting a Soviet invasion in November 1939.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpring1986207-226_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpring1986207-226-81">[79]</a></sup> The resulting <a href="/wiki/Winter_War" title="Winter War">Winter War</a> ended in March 1940 with <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Peace_Treaty" title="Moscow Peace Treaty">Finnish concessions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHanhim.C3.A4ki199712_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanhim.C3.A4ki199712-82">[80]</a></sup> Britain and France, treating the Soviet attack on Finland as tantamount to its entering the war on the side of the Germans, responded to the Soviet invasion by supporting the USSR's expulsion from the League of Nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMurrayMillett200155.E2.80.936_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMurrayMillett200155.E2.80.936-80">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 1940, the Soviet Union forcibly annexed <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_the_Baltic_states_(1940)" title="Soviet occupation of the Baltic states (1940)">Estonia, Latvia and Lithuania</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBilinsky19999_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBilinsky19999-79">[77]</a></sup> and the disputed Romanian regions of <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina" title="Soviet occupation of Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina">Bessarabia, Northern Bukovina and Hertza</a>. Meanwhile, Nazi-Soviet political rapprochement and economic co-operation<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2006367.2C_376.2C_379.2C_417_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2006367.2C_376.2C_379.2C_417-83">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnyder2010118ff_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder2010118ff-84">[82]</a></sup> gradually stalled,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKoch1983_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKoch1983-85">[83]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2016)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoberts200656_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts200656-86">[84]</a></sup> and both states began preparations for war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoberts200659_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts200659-87">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Western_Europe_(1940–41)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_Europe_.281940.E2.80.9341.29">Western Europe (1940–41)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Western Front (World War II)">Western Front (World War II)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maginot_Line_ln-en_svg.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="537" data-file-width="674" height="263" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Maginot_Line_ln-en_svg.svg/330px-Maginot_Line_ln-en_svg.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Maginot_Line_ln-en_svg.svg/495px-Maginot_Line_ln-en_svg.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Maginot_Line_ln-en_svg.svg/660px-Maginot_Line_ln-en_svg.svg.png 2x" width="330"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maginot_Line_ln-en_svg.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the French <a href="/wiki/Maginot_Line" title="Maginot Line">Maginot Line</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In April 1940, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Weser%C3%BCbung" title="Operation Weserübung">Germany invaded Denmark and Norway</a> to protect shipments of <a href="/wiki/Swedish_iron-ore_mining_during_World_War_II" title="Swedish iron-ore mining during World War II">iron ore from Sweden</a>, which the Allies were <a href="/wiki/Operation_Wilfred" title="Operation Wilfred">attempting to cut off</a> by unilaterally mining neutral Norwegian waters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> capitulated after a few hours, and <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Campaign" title="Norwegian Campaign">despite Allied support</a>, during which the important harbour of <a href="/wiki/Narvik" title="Narvik">Narvik</a> temporarily was recaptured from the Germans, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> was conquered within two months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECommager20049_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECommager20049-89">[87]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Norway_Debate" title="Norway Debate">British discontent over the Norwegian campaign</a> led to the replacement of the British Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Neville_Chamberlain" title="Neville Chamberlain">Neville Chamberlain</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> on 10 May 1940.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReynolds200676_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReynolds200676-90">[88]</a></sup></p>
