<p>Germany <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_France" title="Battle of France">launched an offensive against France</a> and, adhering to the <a href="/wiki/Manstein_Plan" title="Manstein Plan">Manstein Plan</a> also attacked the neutral nations of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Belgium" title="Battle of Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Netherlands" title="Battle of the Netherlands">the Netherlands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/German_invasion_of_Luxembourg" title="German invasion of Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a> on 10 May 1940.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2008122.E2.80.933_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2008122.E2.80.933-91">[89]</a></sup> That same day British forces landed in <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Iceland" title="Invasion of Iceland">Iceland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/British_occupation_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="British occupation of the Faroe Islands">Faroes</a> to preempt a possible German invasion of the islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup> The U.S., in close co-operation with <a href="/wiki/Henrik_Kauffmann" title="Henrik Kauffmann">the Danish envoy to Washington D.C.</a>, agreed to protect <a href="/wiki/Greenland_in_World_War_II" title="Greenland in World War II">Greenland</a>, laying the political framework for the formal establishment of bases in April 1941. The <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_in_World_War_II" title="Netherlands in World War II">Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belgium_in_World_War_II" title="Belgium in World War II">Belgium</a> were overrun using <a href="/wiki/Blitzkrieg" title="Blitzkrieg">blitzkrieg</a> tactics in a few days and weeks, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer1990721.E2.80.933_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1990721.E2.80.933-93">[91]</a></sup> The French-fortified <a href="/wiki/Maginot_Line" title="Maginot Line">Maginot Line</a> and the main body of the Allied forces which had moved into Belgium were circumvented by a flanking movement through the thickly wooded <a href="/wiki/Ardennes" title="Ardennes">Ardennes</a> region,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeegan199759.E2.80.9360_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan199759.E2.80.9360-94">[92]</a></sup> mistakenly perceived by Allied planners as an impenetrable natural barrier against armoured vehicles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERegan2004152_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERegan2004152-95">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELiddell_Hart197748_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELiddell_Hart197748-96">[94]</a></sup> As a result, the bulk of the Allied armies found themselves trapped in an encirclement and were beaten. The majority were taken prisoner, whilst over 300,000, mostly British and French, were <a href="/wiki/Dunkirk_evacuation" title="Dunkirk evacuation">evacuated from the continent at Dunkirk</a> by early June, although abandoning almost all of their equipment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeegan199766.E2.80.937_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan199766.E2.80.937-97">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 10 June, <a href="/wiki/Italian_invasion_of_France" title="Italian invasion of France">Italy invaded France</a>, declaring war on both France and the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOveryWheatcroft1999207_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOveryWheatcroft1999207-98">[96]</a></sup> Paris fell to the Germans on 14 June and eight days later <a href="/wiki/Armistice_of_22_June_1940" title="Armistice of 22 June 1940">France signed an armistice with Germany</a> and was soon divided into <a href="/wiki/German_military_administration_in_occupied_France_during_World_War_II" title="German military administration in occupied France during World War II">German</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_occupation_of_France" title="Italian occupation of France">Italian occupation zones</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUmbreit1991311_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUmbreit1991311-99">[97]</a></sup> and an unoccupied <a href="/wiki/Rump_state" title="Rump state">rump state</a> under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vichy_Regime" title="Vichy Regime">Vichy Regime</a>, which, though officially neutral, was generally aligned with Germany. France kept its fleet but the British feared the Germans would seize it, so on 3 July, the British <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Mers-el-K%C3%A9bir" title="Attack on Mers-el-Kébir">attacked it</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrown2004xxx_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrown2004xxx-100">[98]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:View_from_St_Paul%27s_Cathedral_after_the_Blitz.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="514" data-file-width="634" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/View_from_St_Paul%27s_Cathedral_after_the_Blitz.jpg/220px-View_from_St_Paul%27s_Cathedral_after_the_Blitz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/View_from_St_Paul%27s_Cathedral_after_the_Blitz.jpg/330px-View_from_St_Paul%27s_Cathedral_after_the_Blitz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/View_from_St_Paul%27s_Cathedral_after_the_Blitz.jpg/440px-View_from_St_Paul%27s_Cathedral_after_the_Blitz.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:View_from_St_Paul%27s_Cathedral_after_the_Blitz.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> after the German <a href="/wiki/The_Blitz" title="The Blitz"><i>Blitz</i></a>, 29 December 1940</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Britain" title="Battle of Britain">Battle of Britain</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeegan1997.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DTF8kcx9hTssC.26pg.3DPA72_72.5D_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan1997.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DTF8kcx9hTssC.26pg.3DPA72_72.5D-101">[99]</a></sup> began in early July with <a href="/wiki/Kanalkampf" title="Kanalkampf">Luftwaffe attacks on shipping and harbours</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Murray_BoB_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Murray_BoB-102">[100]</a></sup> On 19 July, Hitler again publicly offered to end the war, saying he had no desire to destroy the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>. The United Kingdom rejected this ultimatum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibiblio_1940_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-ibiblio_1940-103">[101]</a></sup> The main <a href="/wiki/Adlertag" title="Adlertag">German air superiority campaign</a> started in August but failed to defeat <a href="/wiki/RAF_Fighter_Command" title="RAF Fighter Command">RAF Fighter Command</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Operation_Sea_Lion" title="Operation Sea Lion">proposed invasion</a> was postponed indefinitely on 17 September. The German <a href="/wiki/Strategic_bombing" title="Strategic bombing">strategic bombing</a> offensive intensified as night attacks on London and other cities in <a href="/wiki/The_Blitz" title="The Blitz">the Blitz</a>, but largely failed to disrupt the British war effort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Murray_BoB_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-Murray_BoB-102">[100]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Heinkel_He_111_during_the_Battle_of_Britain.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="676" data-file-width="800" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Heinkel_He_111_during_the_Battle_of_Britain.jpg/220px-Heinkel_He_111_during_the_Battle_of_Britain.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Heinkel_He_111_during_the_Battle_of_Britain.jpg/330px-Heinkel_He_111_during_the_Battle_of_Britain.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Heinkel_He_111_during_the_Battle_of_Britain.jpg/440px-Heinkel_He_111_during_the_Battle_of_Britain.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Heinkel_He_111_during_the_Battle_of_Britain.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
German <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heinkel_He_111" title="Heinkel He 111">Heinkel He 111</a> bombers during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Britain" title="Battle of Britain">Battle of Britain</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Using newly captured French ports, the German Navy <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Atlantic#.27Happy_Time.27_.28June_1940_.E2.80.93_February_1941.29" title="Battle of the Atlantic">enjoyed success</a> against an over-extended <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>, using <a href="/wiki/U-boat" title="U-boat">U-boats</a> against British shipping in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Atlantic" title="Battle of the Atlantic">Atlantic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup> The British scored a significant victory on 27 May 1941 by <a href="/wiki/Last_battle_of_the_battleship_Bismarck" title="Last battle of the battleship Bismarck">sinking the German battleship <i>Bismarck</i></a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup> Perhaps most importantly, during the Battle of Britain the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> had successfully resisted the Luftwaffe's assault, and the German bombing campaign largely ended in May 1941.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001108.E2.80.939_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001108.E2.80.939-106">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>Throughout this period, the neutral United States took measures to assist China and the Western Allies. In November 1939, the American <a href="/wiki/Neutrality_Acts_of_1930s" title="Neutrality Acts of 1930s">Neutrality Act</a> was amended to allow <a href="/wiki/Cash_and_carry_(World_War_II)" title="Cash and carry (World War II)">"cash and carry"</a> purchases by the Allies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOveryWheatcroft1999328.E2.80.9330_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOveryWheatcroft1999328.E2.80.9330-107">[105]</a></sup> In 1940, following the German capture of Paris, the size of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> was <a href="/wiki/Two-Ocean_Navy_Act" title="Two-Ocean Navy Act">significantly increased</a>. In September, the United States further agreed to a <a href="/wiki/Destroyers_for_Bases_Agreement" title="Destroyers for Bases Agreement">trade of American destroyers for British bases</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaingot199452_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaingot199452-108">[106]</a></sup> Still, a large majority of the American public continued to oppose any direct military intervention into the conflict well into 1941.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECantril1940390_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECantril1940390-109">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although Roosevelt had promised to keep the United States out of the war, he nevertheless took concrete steps to prepare for war. In December 1940 he accused Hitler of planning world conquest and ruled out negotiations as useless, calling for the US to become an "<a href="/wiki/Arsenal_of_Democracy" title="Arsenal of Democracy">arsenal of democracy</a>" and promoted the passage of <a href="/wiki/Lend-Lease" title="Lend-Lease">Lend-Lease</a> aid to support the British war effort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibiblio_1940_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-ibiblio_1940-103">[101]</a></sup> In January 1941 secret high level staff talks with the British began for the purposes of determining how to defeat Germany should the US enter the war. They decided on a number of offensive policies, including an air offensive, the "early elimination" of Italy, raids, support of resistance groups, and the capture of positions to launch an offensive against Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the end of September 1940, the <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Pact" title="Tripartite Pact">Tripartite Pact</a> united Japan, Italy and Germany to formalise the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" title="Axis Powers">Axis Powers</a>. The Tripartite Pact stipulated that any country, with the exception of the Soviet Union, not in the war which attacked any Axis Power would be forced to go to war against all three.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBilhartzElliott2007179_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBilhartzElliott2007179-111">[109]</a></sup> The Axis expanded in November 1940 when Hungary, Slovakia and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Romania" title="Kingdom of Romania">Romania</a> joined the Tripartite Pact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001877_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001877-112">[110]</a></sup> Romania would make a <a href="/wiki/Romania_in_World_War_II" title="Romania in World War II">major contribution</a> (as <a href="/wiki/Hungary_in_World_War_II" title="Hungary in World War II">did Hungary</a>) to the Axis war against the USSR, partially to recapture <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina" title="Soviet occupation of Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina">territory ceded to the USSR</a>, partially to pursue its leader <a href="/wiki/Ion_Antonescu" title="Ion Antonescu">Ion Antonescu</a>'s desire to combat communism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001745.E2.80.936_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDearFoot2001745.E2.80.936-113">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Mediterranean_(1940–41)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mediterranean_.281940.E2.80.9341.29">Mediterranean (1940–41)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_and_Middle_East_theatre_of_World_War_II" title="Mediterranean and Middle East theatre of World War II">Mediterranean and Middle East theatre of World War II</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:9_Div_Tobruk(AWM_020779).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="337" data-file-width="450" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/9_Div_Tobruk%28AWM_020779%29.jpg/220px-9_Div_Tobruk%28AWM_020779%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/9_Div_Tobruk%28AWM_020779%29.jpg/330px-9_Div_Tobruk%28AWM_020779%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/9_Div_Tobruk%28AWM_020779%29.jpg/440px-9_Div_Tobruk%28AWM_020779%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:9_Div_Tobruk(AWM_020779).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Soldiers of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire_in_World_War_II" title="British Empire in World War II">British Commonwealth forces</a> from the Australian Army's <a href="/wiki/9th_Division_(Australia)" title="9th Division (Australia)">9th Division</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Tobruk" title="Siege of Tobruk">Siege of Tobruk</a>; <a href="/wiki/North_African_Campaign" title="North African Campaign">North African Campaign</a>, August 1941</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Italy began operations in the Mediterranean, initiating a <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Malta_(World_War_II)" title="Siege of Malta (World War II)">siege of Malta</a> in June, <a href="/wiki/Italian_conquest_of_British_Somaliland" title="Italian conquest of British Somaliland">conquering British Somaliland</a> in August, and <a href="/wiki/Italian_invasion_of_Egypt" title="Italian invasion of Egypt">making an incursion into British-held Egypt</a> in September 1940. In October 1940, Italy started the <a href="/wiki/Greco-Italian_War" title="Greco-Italian War">Greco-Italian War</a> because of Mussolini's jealousy of Hitler's success but within days was repulsed with few territorial gains and a stalemate soon occurred.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClogg2002118_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClogg2002118-114">[112]</a></sup> The United Kingdom responded to Greek requests for assistance by sending troops to Crete and providing air support to Greece. Hitler decided that when the weather improved he would take action against Greece to assist the Italians and prevent the British from gaining a foothold in the Balkans, to strike against the British naval dominance of the Mediterranean, and to secure his hold on Romanian oil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 1940, British Commonwealth forces began counter-offensives against <a href="/wiki/Operation_Compass" title="Operation Compass">Italian forces in Egypt</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_African_Campaign_(World_War_II)#Allied_counter-offensive" title="East African Campaign (World War II)">Italian East Africa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJowett20019.E2.80.9310_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJowett20019.E2.80.9310-116">[114]</a></sup> The offensive in North Africa was highly successful and by early February 1941 Italy had lost control of eastern Libya and large numbers of Italian troops had been taken prisoner. The <a href="/wiki/Regia_Marina" title="Regia Marina">Italian Navy</a> also suffered significant defeats, with the Royal Navy putting three Italian battleships out of commission by a <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Taranto" title="Battle of Taranto">carrier attack at Taranto</a>, and neutralising several more warships at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cape_Matapan" title="Battle of Cape Matapan">Battle of Cape Matapan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson2006106_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson2006106-117">[115]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:E_003743_E.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="579" data-file-width="800" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/E_003743_E.jpg/220px-E_003743_E.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/E_003743_E.jpg/330px-E_003743_E.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/E_003743_E.jpg/440px-E_003743_E.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:E_003743_E.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Captured German <a href="/wiki/Afrika_Korps" title="Afrika Korps">Afrika Korps</a> soldiers, December 1941</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Germans soon intervened to assist Italy. Hitler <a href="/wiki/Operation_Sonnenblume" title="Operation Sonnenblume">sent German forces to Libya</a> in February, and by the end of March the Axis had <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axis_desert_offensive_(1941)" title="Axis desert offensive (1941)">launched an offensive</a> which drove back the Commonwealth forces which had been weakened to support Greece.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaurier20017.E2.80.938_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaurier20017.E2.80.938-118">[116]</a></sup> In under a month, Commonwealth forces were pushed back into Egypt with the exception of the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Tobruk" title="Siege of Tobruk">besieged port of Tobruk</a> that fell later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMurrayMillett2001263.E2.80.937_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMurrayMillett2001263.E2.80.937-119">[117]</a></sup> The Commonwealth <a href="/wiki/Operation_Brevity" title="Operation Brevity">attempted to dislodge Axis forces in May</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Battleaxe" title="Operation Battleaxe">again in June</a>, but failed on both occasions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacksey199761.E2.80.933_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacksey199761.E2.80.933-120">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>By late March 1941, following <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>'s signing of the <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Pact" title="Tripartite Pact">Tripartite Pact</a>, the Germans were in position to intervene in Greece. Plans were changed, however, because of developments in neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>. The Yugoslav government had signed the Tripartite Pact on 25 March, only to be overthrown two days later by a <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Yugoslav coup d'état">British-encouraged coup</a>. Hitler viewed the new regime as hostile and immediately decided to eliminate it. On 6 April Germany simultaneously invaded both <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Yugoslavia" title="Invasion of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Greece" title="Battle of Greece">Greece</a>, making rapid progress and forcing both nations to surrender within the month. The British were driven from the Balkans after Germany <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Crete" title="Battle of Crete">conquered the Greek island of Crete</a> by the end of May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeinberg2005229_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeinberg2005229-121">[119]</a></sup> Although the Axis victory was swift, bitter partisan warfare subsequently broke out against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axis_occupation_of_Yugoslavia" title="Axis occupation of Yugoslavia">Axis occupation of Yugoslavia</a>, which continued until the end of the war.</p>
<p>The Allies did have some successes during this time. In the Middle East, Commonwealth forces first <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Iraqi_War" title="Anglo-Iraqi War">quashed an uprising in Iraq</a> which had been supported by German aircraft from bases within Vichy-controlled <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Mandate_of_Syria" title="French Mandate of Syria">Syria</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWatson200380_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWatson200380-122">[120]</a></sup> then, with the assistance of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_French" title="Free French">Free French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria%E2%80%93Lebanon_Campaign" title="Syria–Lebanon Campaign">invaded Syria and Lebanon</a> to prevent further such occurrences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson2006154_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson2006154-123">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Axis_attack_on_the_USSR_(1941)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Axis_attack_on_the_USSR_.281941.29">Axis attack on the USSR (1941)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front (World War II)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">Operation Barbarossa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Einsatzgruppen" title="Einsatzgruppen">Einsatzgruppen</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_casualties_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="World War II casualties of the Soviet Union">World War II casualties of the Soviet Union</a>, and <a href="/wiki/German_mistreatment_of_Soviet_prisoners_of_war" title="German mistreatment of Soviet prisoners of war">German mistreatment of Soviet prisoners of war</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:249px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Second_world_war_europe_animation_small.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="257" data-file-width="247" height="257" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/19/Second_world_war_europe_animation_small.gif" width="247"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Second_world_war_europe_animation_small.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/European_theatre_of_World_War_II" title="European theatre of World War II">European theatre of World War II</a> animation map, 1939–1945 — Red: <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Western Allies</a> and Soviet Union after 1941; Green: <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> before 1941; Blue: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" title="Axis Powers">Axis Powers</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With the situation in Europe and Asia relatively stable, Germany, Japan, and the Soviet Union made preparations. With the Soviets wary of mounting tensions with Germany and the Japanese planning to take advantage of the European War by seizing resource-rich European possessions in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, the two powers signed the <a href="/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Japanese_Neutrality_Pact" title="Soviet–Japanese Neutrality Pact">Soviet–Japanese Neutrality Pact</a> in April 1941.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGarver1988114_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGarver1988114-124">[122]</a></sup> By contrast, the Germans were steadily making preparations for an attack on the Soviet Union, massing forces on the Soviet border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeinberg2005195_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeinberg2005195-125">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hitler believed that Britain's refusal to end the war was based on the hope that the United States and the Soviet Union would enter the war against Germany sooner or later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMurray1983.5Bhttp:.2F.2Fwww.ibiblio.org.2Fhyperwar.2FAAF.2FAAF-Luftwaffe.2FAAF-Luftwaffe-3.html_69.5D_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMurray1983.5Bhttp:.2F.2Fwww.ibiblio.org.2Fhyperwar.2FAAF.2FAAF-Luftwaffe.2FAAF-Luftwaffe-3.html_69.5D-126">[124]</a></sup> He therefore decided to try to strengthen Germany's relations with the Soviets, or failing that, to attack and eliminate them as a factor. In November 1940, <a href="/wiki/German%E2%80%93Soviet_Axis_talks" title="German–Soviet Axis talks">negotiations took place</a> to determine if the Soviet Union would join the Tripartite Pact. The Soviets showed some interest, but asked for concessions from Finland, Bulgaria, Turkey, and Japan that Germany considered unacceptable. On 18 December 1940, Hitler issued the directive to prepare for an invasion of the Soviet Union.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:German_troops_in_Russia,_1941_-_NARA_-_540155.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1973" data-file-width="3000" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/German_troops_in_Russia%2C_1941_-_NARA_-_540155.jpg/220px-German_troops_in_Russia%2C_1941_-_NARA_-_540155.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/German_troops_in_Russia%2C_1941_-_NARA_-_540155.jpg/330px-German_troops_in_Russia%2C_1941_-_NARA_-_540155.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/German_troops_in_Russia%2C_1941_-_NARA_-_540155.jpg/440px-German_troops_in_Russia%2C_1941_-_NARA_-_540155.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:German_troops_in_Russia,_1941_-_NARA_-_540155.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
German soldiers during the invasion of the Soviet Union by the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a>, 1941</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 22 June 1941, Germany, supported by Italy and Romania, invaded the Soviet Union in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">Operation Barbarossa</a>, with Germany accusing the Soviets of plotting against them. They were joined shortly by Finland and Hungary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Events1941_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-Events1941-127">[125]</a></sup> The primary targets of this surprise offensive<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESella1978_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESella1978-128">[126]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2016)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup> were the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_region" title="Baltic region">Baltic region</a>, Moscow and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Strategic_goal_(military)" title="Strategic goal (military)">ultimate goal</a> of ending the 1941 campaign near the <a href="/wiki/A-A_line" title="A-A line">Arkhangelsk-Astrakhan line</a>, from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caspian_sea" title="Caspian sea">Caspian</a> to the <a href="/wiki/White_Sea" title="White Sea">White Seas</a>. Hitler's objectives were to eliminate the Soviet Union as a military power, exterminate Communism, generate <i><a href="/wiki/Lebensraum" title="Lebensraum">Lebensraum</a></i> ("living space")<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200766.E2.80.939_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200766.E2.80.939-129">[127]</a></sup> by <a href="/wiki/Generalplan_Ost" title="Generalplan Ost">dispossessing the native population</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESteinberg1995_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESteinberg1995-130">[128]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2016)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and guarantee access to the strategic resources needed to defeat Germany's remaining rivals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHauner1978_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHauner1978-131">[129]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2016)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Although the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> was preparing for strategic <a href="/wiki/Counter-offensive" title="Counter-offensive">counter-offensives</a> before the war,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoberts1995_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts1995-132">[130]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2016)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <i>Barbarossa</i> forced the <a href="/wiki/Stavka" title="Stavka">Soviet supreme command</a> to adopt a <a href="/wiki/Strategic_defence" title="Strategic defence">strategic defence</a>. During the summer, the Axis made significant gains into Soviet territory, inflicting immense losses in both personnel and materiel. By the middle of August, however, the German <a href="/wiki/Oberkommando_des_Heeres" title="Oberkommando des Heeres">Army High Command</a> decided to <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Smolensk_(1941)" title="Battle of Smolensk (1941)">suspend the offensive</a> of a considerably depleted <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_Centre" title="Army Group Centre">Army Group Centre</a>, and to divert the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2nd_Panzer_Group" title="2nd Panzer Group">2nd Panzer Group</a> to reinforce troops advancing towards central Ukraine and Leningrad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilt1981_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilt1981-133">[131]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2016)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kiev_(1941)" title="Battle of Kiev (1941)">Kiev offensive</a> was overwhelmingly successful, resulting in encirclement and elimination of four Soviet armies, and made possible further <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Campaign" title="Crimean Campaign">advance into Crimea</a> and industrially developed Eastern Ukraine (the <a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_Kharkov" title="First Battle of Kharkov">First Battle of Kharkov</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEErickson2003114.E2.80.9337_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEErickson2003114.E2.80.9337-134">[132]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="366" data-file-width="600" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg/220px-RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg/330px-RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg/440px-RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Soviet civilians in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leningrad" title="Leningrad">Leningrad</a> leaving destroyed houses, after a German bombardment of the city; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Leningrad" title="Battle of Leningrad">Battle of Leningrad</a>, 10 December 1942</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The diversion of three quarters of the Axis troops and the majority of their air forces from France and the central Mediterranean to the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGlantz20019_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGlantz20019-135">[133]</a></sup> prompted Britain to reconsider its <a href="/wiki/Grand_strategy" title="Grand strategy">grand strategy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFarrell1993_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFarrell1993-136">[134]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2016)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In July, the UK and the Soviet Union formed a <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Soviet_Agreement" title="Anglo-Soviet Agreement">military alliance against Germany</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeeble199029_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeeble199029-137">[135]</a></sup> The British and Soviets <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Soviet_invasion_of_Iran" title="Anglo-Soviet invasion of Iran">invaded neutral Iran</a> to secure the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Corridor" title="Persian Corridor">Persian Corridor</a> and Iran's <a href="/wiki/Oil_field" title="Oil field">oil fields</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBueno_de_MesquitaSmithSiversonMorrow2003425_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBueno_de_MesquitaSmithSiversonMorrow2003425-138">[136]</a></sup> In August, the United Kingdom and the United States jointly issued the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Charter" title="Atlantic Charter">Atlantic Charter</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012220_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012220-139">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>By October Axis <a href="/wiki/Operational_objective" title="Operational objective">operational objectives</a> in Ukraine and the Baltic region were achieved, with only the sieges of <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Leningrad" title="Siege of Leningrad">Leningrad</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKleinfeld1983_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKleinfeld1983-140">[138]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2016)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Sevastopol_(1941%E2%80%9342)" title="Siege of Sevastopol (1941–42)">Sevastopol</a> continuing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJukes2001113_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJukes2001113-141">[139]</a></sup> A major <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Moscow" title="Battle of Moscow">offensive against Moscow</a> was renewed; after two months of fierce battles in increasingly harsh weather the German army almost reached the outer suburbs of Moscow, where the exhausted troops<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup> were forced to suspend their offensive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReinhardt1992227_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReinhardt1992227-143">[141]</a></sup> Large territorial gains were made by Axis forces, but their campaign had failed to achieve its main objectives: two key cities remained in Soviet hands, the Soviet <a href="/wiki/Military_capability" title="Military capability">capability to resist</a> was not broken, and the Soviet Union retained a considerable part of its military potential. The <i>blitzkrieg</i> <a href="/wiki/Phase_(combat)" title="Phase (combat)">phase</a> of the war in Europe had ended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMilward1964_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMilward1964-144">[142]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2016)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>By early December, freshly mobilised <a href="/wiki/Military_reserve_force" title="Military reserve force">reserves</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERotundo1986_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERotundo1986-145">[143]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2016)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup> allowed the Soviets to achieve numerical parity with Axis troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGlantz200126_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGlantz200126-146">[144]</a></sup> This, as well as <a href="/wiki/Richard_Sorge#Wartime_intelligence_supplied_by_the_Sorge_Ring" title="Richard Sorge">intelligence data</a> which established that a minimal number of Soviet troops in the East would be sufficient to deter any attack by the Japanese <a href="/wiki/Kwantung_Army" title="Kwantung Army">Kwantung Army</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGarthoff1969_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGarthoff1969-147">[145]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2016)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup> allowed the Soviets to begin a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_Offensive_(1941%E2%80%931942)" title="Soviet Offensive (1941–1942)">massive counter-offensive</a> that started on 5 December all along the front and pushed German troops 100–250 kilometres (62–155 mi) west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="War_breaks_out_in_the_Pacific_(1941)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="War_breaks_out_in_the_Pacific_.281941.29">War breaks out in the Pacific (1941)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">Pacific War</a></div>
<p>In 1939, the United States had renounced its trade treaty with Japan; and, beginning with an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aviation_gasoline" title="Aviation gasoline">aviation gasoline</a> ban in July 1940, Japan became subject to increasing economic pressure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibiblio_1940_103-2"><a href="#cite_note-ibiblio_1940-103">[101]</a></sup> During this time, Japan launched its <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Changsha_(1939)" title="Battle of Changsha (1939)">first attack against Changsha</a>, a strategically important Chinese city, but was repulsed by late September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJowettAndrew200214_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJowettAndrew200214-149">[147]</a></sup> Despite <a href="/wiki/1939%E2%80%9340_Winter_Offensive" title="1939–40 Winter Offensive">several offensives</a> by both sides, the war between China and Japan was stalemated by 1940. To increase pressure on China by blocking supply routes, and to better position Japanese forces in the event of a war with the Western powers, Japan invaded and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_French_Indochina" title="Japanese invasion of French Indochina">occupied northern Indochina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOveryWheatcroft1999289_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOveryWheatcroft1999289-150">[148]</a></sup> Afterwards, the United States <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embargo" title="Embargo">embargoed</a> iron, steel and mechanical parts against Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorison200260_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorison200260-151">[149]</a></sup> Other sanctions soon followed.</p>
<p>Chinese nationalist forces launched a large-scale <a href="/wiki/1939%E2%80%9340_Winter_Offensive" title="1939–40 Winter Offensive">counter-offensive</a> in early 1940. In August, <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">Chinese communists</a> launched an <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Regiments_Offensive" title="Hundred Regiments Offensive">offensive in Central China</a>; in retaliation, Japan instituted <a href="/wiki/Three_Alls_Policy" title="Three Alls Policy">harsh measures</a> in occupied areas to reduce human and material resources for the communists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJoes2004224_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJoes2004224-152">[150]</a></sup> Continued antipathy between Chinese communist and nationalist forces <a href="/wiki/New_Fourth_Army_incident" title="New Fourth Army incident">culminated in armed clashes in January 1941</a>, effectively ending their co-operation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFairbankGoldman2006320_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFairbankGoldman2006320-153">[151]</a></sup> In March, the Japanese 11th army attacked the headquarters of the Chinese 19th army but was repulsed during <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Shanggao" title="Battle of Shanggao">Battle of Shanggao</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHsuChang197130_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHsuChang197130-154">[152]</a></sup> In September, Japan attempted to <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Changsha_(1941)" title="Battle of Changsha (1941)">take the city of Changsha</a> again and clashed with Chinese nationalist forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHsuChang197133_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHsuChang197133-155">[153]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carrier_shokaku.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4232" data-file-width="5594" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Carrier_shokaku.jpg/220px-Carrier_shokaku.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Carrier_shokaku.jpg/330px-Carrier_shokaku.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Carrier_shokaku.jpg/440px-Carrier_shokaku.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carrier_shokaku.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_A6M2" title="Mitsubishi A6M2">Mitsubishi A6M2</a> "Zero" fighters on the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Navy" title="Imperial Japanese Navy">Imperial Japanese Navy</a> aircraft carrier <a href="/wiki/Japanese_aircraft_carrier_Sh%C5%8Dkaku" title="Japanese aircraft carrier Shōkaku"><i>Shōkaku</i></a>, just before the attack on <a href="/wiki/Naval_Station_Pearl_Harbor" title="Naval Station Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>German successes in Europe encouraged Japan to increase pressure on European governments in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>. The Dutch government agreed to provide Japan some oil supplies from the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a>, but negotiations for additional access to their resources ended in failure in June 1941.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup> In July 1941 Japan sent troops to southern Indochina, thus threatening British and Dutch possessions in the Far East. The United States, United Kingdom and other Western governments reacted to this move with a freeze on Japanese assets and a total oil embargo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1975201_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1975201-157">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvansPeattie2012456_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvansPeattie2012456-158">[156]</a></sup> At the same time, Japan was <a href="/wiki/Kantokuen" title="Kantokuen">planning an invasion of the Soviet Far East</a>, intending to capitalize off the German invasion in the west, but abandoned the operation after the sanctions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since early 1941 the United States and Japan had been engaged in negotiations in an attempt to improve their strained relations and end the war in China. During these negotiations Japan advanced a number of proposals which were dismissed by the Americans as inadequate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAWWIIcp5_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-USAWWIIcp5-160">[158]</a></sup> At the same time the US, Britain, and the Netherlands engaged in secret discussions for the joint defence of their territories, in the event of a Japanese attack against any of them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAWWIIcp4_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-USAWWIIcp4-161">[159]</a></sup> Roosevelt reinforced <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_the_Philippines" title="Commonwealth of the Philippines">the Philippines (an American protectorate scheduled for independence in 1946)</a> and warned Japan that the US would react to Japanese attacks against any "neighboring countries".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAWWIIcp4_161-1"><a href="#cite_note-USAWWIIcp4-161">[159]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_USS_Arizona_(BB-39)_burning_after_the_Japanese_attack_on_Pearl_Harbor_-_NARA_195617_-_Edit.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2326" data-file-width="2940" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/The_USS_Arizona_%28BB-39%29_burning_after_the_Japanese_attack_on_Pearl_Harbor_-_NARA_195617_-_Edit.jpg/220px-The_USS_Arizona_%28BB-39%29_burning_after_the_Japanese_attack_on_Pearl_Harbor_-_NARA_195617_-_Edit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/The_USS_Arizona_%28BB-39%29_burning_after_the_Japanese_attack_on_Pearl_Harbor_-_NARA_195617_-_Edit.jpg/330px-The_USS_Arizona_%28BB-39%29_burning_after_the_Japanese_attack_on_Pearl_Harbor_-_NARA_195617_-_Edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/The_USS_Arizona_%28BB-39%29_burning_after_the_Japanese_attack_on_Pearl_Harbor_-_NARA_195617_-_Edit.jpg/440px-The_USS_Arizona_%28BB-39%29_burning_after_the_Japanese_attack_on_Pearl_Harbor_-_NARA_195617_-_Edit.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_USS_Arizona_(BB-39)_burning_after_the_Japanese_attack_on_Pearl_Harbor_-_NARA_195617_-_Edit.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/USS_Arizona_(BB-39)" title="USS Arizona (BB-39)">USS <i>Arizona</i></a> during the Japanese surprise air attack on the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Pacific_Fleet" title="United States Pacific Fleet">American pacific fleet</a>, 7 December 1941</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Frustrated at the lack of progress and feeling the pinch of the American-British-Dutch sanctions, Japan prepared for war. On 20 November a new government under Hideki Tojo presented an interim proposal as its final offer. It called for the end of American aid to China and for the supply of oil and other resources to Japan. In exchange Japan promised not to launch any attacks in Southeast Asia and to withdraw its forces from southern Indochina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAWWIIcp5_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-USAWWIIcp5-160">[158]</a></sup> The American counter-proposal of 26 November required that Japan evacuate all of China without conditions and conclude non-aggression pacts with all Pacific powers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup> That meant Japan was essentially forced to choose between abandoning its ambitions in China, or seizing the natural resources it needed in the Dutch East Indies by force;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[161]</a></sup> the Japanese military did not consider the former an option, and many officers considered the oil embargo an unspoken declaration of war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELightbody2004125_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELightbody2004125-164">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>Japan planned to rapidly seize European colonies in Asia to create a large defensive perimeter stretching into the Central Pacific; the Japanese would then be free to exploit the resources of Southeast Asia while exhausting the over-stretched Allies by fighting a defensive war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[163]</a></sup> To prevent American intervention while securing the perimeter it was further planned to neutralise the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Pacific_Fleet" title="United States Pacific Fleet">United States Pacific Fleet</a> and the American military presence in the Philippines from the outset.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWood200711.E2.80.932_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWood200711.E2.80.932-166">[164]</a></sup> On 7 December 1941 (8 December in Asian time zones), Japan attacked British and American holdings with near-simultaneous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_expansion_(1941%E2%80%931942)" title="Japanese expansion (1941–1942)">offensives against Southeast Asia and the Central Pacific</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWohlstetter1962341.E2.80.933_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWohlstetter1962341.E2.80.933-167">[165]</a></sup> These included an <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attack on the American fleet at Pearl Harbor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines_Campaign_(1941%E2%80%9342)" title="Philippines Campaign (1941–42)">the Philippines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malayan_Campaign" title="Malayan Campaign">landings in Thailand and Malaya</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWohlstetter1962341.E2.80.933_167-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWohlstetter1962341.E2.80.933-167">[165]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hong_Kong" title="Battle of Hong Kong">battle of Hong Kong</a>.</p>
<p>These attacks led the <a href="/wiki/United_States_declaration_of_war_on_Japan" title="United States declaration of war on Japan">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_declaration_of_war_on_Japan" title="United Kingdom declaration of war on Japan">Britain</a>, China, Australia and several other states to formally declare war on Japan, whereas the Soviet Union, being heavily involved in large-scale hostilities with European Axis countries, maintained its neutrality agreement with Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[166]</a></sup> Germany, followed by the other Axis states, declared war on the United States<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[167]</a></sup> in solidarity with Japan, citing as justification the American attacks on German war vessels that had been ordered by Roosevelt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Events1941_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-Events1941-127">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[168]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Axis_advance_stalls_(1942–43)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Axis_advance_stalls_.281942.E2.80.9343.29">Axis advance stalls (1942–43)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Casablanca-Conference.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="578" data-file-width="640" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Casablanca-Conference.jpg/220px-Casablanca-Conference.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Casablanca-Conference.jpg/330px-Casablanca-Conference.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Casablanca-Conference.jpg/440px-Casablanca-Conference.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Casablanca-Conference.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Seated at the <a href="/wiki/Casablanca_Conference" title="Casablanca Conference">Casablanca Conference</a>; US President <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> and British PM <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, January 1943</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 1 January 1942, the <a href="/wiki/Four_Policemen" title="Four Policemen">Allied Big Four</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBosworthMaiolo2015313.E2.80.93314_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBosworthMaiolo2015313.E2.80.93314-171">[169]</a></sup>—the Soviet Union, China, Britain and the United States—and 22 smaller or exiled governments issued the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_by_United_Nations" title="Declaration by United Nations">Declaration by United Nations</a>, thereby affirming the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Charter" title="Atlantic Charter">Atlantic Charter</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMingstKarns200722_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMingstKarns200722-172">[170]</a></sup> and agreeing to not to sign a <a href="/wiki/Separate_peace" title="Separate peace">separate peace</a> with the Axis powers.</p>
<p>During 1942, Allied officials debated on the appropriate <a href="/wiki/Grand_strategy" title="Grand strategy">grand strategy</a> to pursue. All agreed that <a href="/wiki/Europe_first" title="Europe first">defeating Germany</a> was the primary objective. The Americans favoured a straightforward, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Sledgehammer" title="Operation Sledgehammer">large-scale attack</a> on Germany through France. The Soviets were also demanding a second front. The British, on the other hand, argued that military operations should target peripheral areas to wear out German strength, leading to increasing demoralisation, and bolster resistance forces. Germany itself would be subject to a heavy bombing campaign. An offensive against Germany would then be launched primarily by Allied armour without using large-scale armies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup> Eventually, the British persuaded the Americans that a landing in France was infeasible in 1942 and they should instead focus on driving the Axis out of North Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/Casablanca_Conference" title="Casablanca Conference">Casablanca Conference</a> in early 1943, the Allies reiterated the statements issued in the 1942 Declaration by the United Nations, and demanded the <a href="/wiki/Unconditional_surrender" title="Unconditional surrender">unconditional surrender</a> of their enemies. The British and Americans agreed to continue to press the initiative in the Mediterranean by invading Sicily to fully secure the Mediterranean supply routes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup> Although the British argued for further operations in the Balkans to bring Turkey into the war, in May 1943, the Americans extracted a British commitment to limit Allied operations in the Mediterranean to an invasion of the Italian mainland and to invade France in 1944.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[174]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span id="Pacific_(1942–43)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Pacific_.281942.E2.80.9343.29">Pacific (1942–43)</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Second_world_war_asia_1937-1942_map_en6.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="998" data-file-width="1298" height="269" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Second_world_war_asia_1937-1942_map_en6.png/350px-Second_world_war_asia_1937-1942_map_en6.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Second_world_war_asia_1937-1942_map_en6.png/525px-Second_world_war_asia_1937-1942_map_en6.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Second_world_war_asia_1937-1942_map_en6.png/700px-Second_world_war_asia_1937-1942_map_en6.png 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Second_world_war_asia_1937-1942_map_en6.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of Japanese military advances, until mid-1942</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By the end of April 1942, Japan and its ally Thailand had almost fully conquered <a href="/wiki/Japanese_conquest_of_Burma" title="Japanese conquest of Burma">Burma</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Malaya" title="Battle of Malaya">Malaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies_campaign" title="Dutch East Indies campaign">the Dutch East Indies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Singapore" title="Battle of Singapore">Singapore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rabaul" title="Rabaul">Rabaul</a>, inflicting severe losses on Allied troops and taking a large number of prisoners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012247.E2.80.93267.2C_345_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012247.E2.80.93267.2C_345-177">[175]</a></sup> Despite stubborn <a href="/wiki/Philippines_Campaign_(1941%E2%80%9342)" title="Philippines Campaign (1941–42)">resistance</a> by Filipino and US forces, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Commonwealth" title="Philippine Commonwealth">Philippine Commonwealth</a> was eventually captured in May 1942, forcing its government into exile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewis1953p._529_.28Table_11.29_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewis1953p._529_.28Table_11.29-178">[176]</a></sup> On 16 April, in Burma, 7,000 British soldiers were encircled by the Japanese 33rd Division during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Yenangyaung" title="Battle of Yenangyaung">Battle of Yenangyaung</a> and rescued by the Chinese 38th Division.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlim195671.E2.80.934_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlim195671.E2.80.934-179">[177]</a></sup> Japanese forces also achieved naval victories in the <a href="/wiki/Sinking_of_Prince_of_Wales_and_Repulse" title="Sinking of Prince of Wales and Repulse">South China Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Java_Sea" title="Battle of the Java Sea">Java Sea</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean_raid_(1942)" title="Indian Ocean raid (1942)">Indian Ocean</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrove1995362_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrove1995362-180">[178]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Darwin" title="Bombing of Darwin">bombed the Allied naval base</a> at <a href="/wiki/Darwin,_Northern_Territory" title="Darwin, Northern Territory">Darwin</a>, Australia. In January 1942, the only Allied success against Japan was a Chinese <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Changsha_(1942)" title="Battle of Changsha (1942)">victory at Changsha</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECh.27i1992158_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECh.27i1992158-181">[179]</a></sup> These easy victories over unprepared US and European opponents left Japan overconfident, as well as overextended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerez1998145_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerez1998145-182">[180]</a></sup></p>
<p>In early May 1942, Japan initiated operations to <a href="/wiki/Operation_Mo" title="Operation Mo">capture Port Moresby</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amphibious_assault" title="Amphibious assault">amphibious assault</a> and thus sever communications and supply lines between the United States and Australia. The planned invasion was thwarted when an Allied task force, centred on two American fleet carriers, fought Japanese naval forces to a draw in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Coral_Sea" title="Battle of the Coral Sea">Battle of the Coral Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaddox1992111.E2.80.932_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaddox1992111.E2.80.932-183">[181]</a></sup> Japan's next plan, motivated by the earlier <a href="/wiki/Doolittle_Raid" title="Doolittle Raid">Doolittle Raid</a>, was to seize <a href="/wiki/Midway_Atoll" title="Midway Atoll">Midway Atoll</a> and lure American carriers into battle to be eliminated; as a diversion, Japan would also send forces to <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands_Campaign" title="Aleutian Islands Campaign">occupy the Aleutian Islands</a> in Alaska.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESalecker2001186_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESalecker2001186-184">[182]</a></sup> In mid-May, Japan started the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zhejiang-Jiangxi_Campaign" title="Zhejiang-Jiangxi Campaign">Zhejiang-Jiangxi Campaign</a> in China, with the goal of inflicting retribution on the Chinese who aided the surviving American airmen in the Doolittle Raid by destroying air bases and fighting against the Chinese 23rd and 32nd Army Groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[184]</a></sup> In early June, Japan put its operations into action but the Americans, having broken <a href="/wiki/Japanese_naval_codes" title="Japanese naval codes">Japanese naval codes</a> in late May, were fully aware of plans and order of battle, and used this knowledge to achieve a decisive <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Midway" title="Battle of Midway">victory at Midway</a> over the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Navy" title="Imperial Japanese Navy">Imperial Japanese Navy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[185]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marines_rest_in_the_field_on_Guadalcanal.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="740" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Marines_rest_in_the_field_on_Guadalcanal.jpg/220px-Marines_rest_in_the_field_on_Guadalcanal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Marines_rest_in_the_field_on_Guadalcanal.jpg/330px-Marines_rest_in_the_field_on_Guadalcanal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Marines_rest_in_the_field_on_Guadalcanal.jpg/440px-Marines_rest_in_the_field_on_Guadalcanal.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marines_rest_in_the_field_on_Guadalcanal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">US Marines</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Guadalcanal_Campaign" title="Guadalcanal Campaign">Guadalcanal Campaign</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean_theater_of_World_War_II" title="Pacific Ocean theater of World War II">Pacific theatre</a>, 1942</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With its capacity for aggressive action greatly diminished as a result of the Midway battle, Japan chose to focus on a belated attempt to capture <a href="/wiki/Port_Moresby" title="Port Moresby">Port Moresby</a> by an <a href="/wiki/Kokoda_Track_campaign" title="Kokoda Track campaign">overland campaign</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Papua" title="Territory of Papua">Territory of Papua</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeinberg2005339_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeinberg2005339-188">[186]</a></sup> The Americans planned a counter-attack against Japanese positions in the southern <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a>, primarily <a href="/wiki/Guadalcanal" title="Guadalcanal">Guadalcanal</a>, as a first step towards capturing <a href="/wiki/Rabaul" title="Rabaul">Rabaul</a>, the main Japanese base in Southeast Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[187]</a></sup></p>
<p>Both plans started in July, but by mid-September, <a href="/wiki/Guadalcanal_Campaign" title="Guadalcanal Campaign">the Battle for Guadalcanal</a> took priority for the Japanese, and troops in New Guinea were ordered to withdraw from the Port Moresby area to the <a href="/wiki/Oro_Province" title="Oro Province">northern part of the island</a>, where they faced Australian and United States troops in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Buna-Gona" title="Battle of Buna-Gona">Battle of Buna-Gona</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwain2001197_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwain2001197-190">[188]</a></sup> Guadalcanal soon became a focal point for both sides with heavy commitments of troops and ships in the battle for Guadalcanal. By the start of 1943, the Japanese were defeated on the island and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Ke" title="Operation Ke">withdrew their troops</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHane2001340_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHane2001340-191">[189]</a></sup> In Burma, Commonwealth forces mounted two operations. The first, <a href="/wiki/Arakan_Campaign_1942%E2%80%9343" title="Arakan Campaign 1942–43">an offensive into the Arakan region</a> in late 1942, went disastrously, forcing a retreat back to India by May 1943.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarston2005111_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarston2005111-192">[190]</a></sup> The second was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Longcloth" title="Operation Longcloth">insertion of irregular forces</a> behind Japanese front-lines in February which, by the end of April, had achieved mixed results.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrayley20029_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrayley20029-193">[191]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span id="Eastern_Front_(1942–43)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Front_.281942.E2.80.9343.29">Eastern Front (1942–43)</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="287" data-file-width="600" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg/300px-RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg/450px-RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ef/RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> soldiers on the counterattack, during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad" title="Battle of Stalingrad">Battle of Stalingrad</a>, February 1943</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Despite considerable losses, in early 1942 Germany and its allies stopped a major Soviet offensive in central and southern Russia, keeping most territorial gains they had achieved during the previous year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGlantz200131_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGlantz200131-194">[192]</a></sup> In May the Germans defeated Soviet offensives in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Kerch_Peninsula" title="Battle of the Kerch Peninsula">Kerch Peninsula</a> and at <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Kharkov" title="Second Battle of Kharkov">Kharkov</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERead2004764_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERead2004764-195">[193]</a></sup> and then launched their main <a href="/wiki/Case_Blue" title="Case Blue">summer offensive</a> against southern Russia in June 1942, to seize the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baku_Oil_Fields" title="Baku Oil Fields">oil fields of the Caucasus</a> and occupy <a href="/wiki/Kuban" title="Kuban">Kuban</a> <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppe</a>, while maintaining positions on the northern and central areas of the front. The Germans split <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_South" title="Army Group South">Army Group South</a> into two groups: <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_A" title="Army Group A">Army Group A</a> advanced to the lower <a href="/wiki/Don_River_(Russia)" title="Don River (Russia)">Don River</a> and struck south-east to the Caucasus, while <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_B" title="Army Group B">Army Group B</a> headed towards the <a href="/wiki/Volga_River" title="Volga River">Volga River</a>. The Soviets decided to make their stand at Stalingrad on the Volga.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies2006p._100_.282008_ed..29_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2006p._100_.282008_ed..29-196">[194]</a></sup></p>
<p>By mid-November, the Germans had <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad" title="Battle of Stalingrad">nearly taken Stalingrad</a> in bitter <a href="/wiki/Urban_warfare" title="Urban warfare">street fighting</a> when the Soviets began their second winter counter-offensive, starting with an <a href="/wiki/Operation_Uranus" title="Operation Uranus">encirclement of German forces at Stalingrad</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeevor1998239.E2.80.9365_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor1998239.E2.80.9365-197">[195]</a></sup> and an assault on the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Mars" title="Operation Mars">Rzhev salient near Moscow</a>, though the latter failed disastrously.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack2003119_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2003119-198">[196]</a></sup> By early February 1943, the German Army had taken tremendous losses; German troops at Stalingrad had been forced to surrender,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeevor1998383.E2.80.9391_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor1998383.E2.80.9391-199">[197]</a></sup> and the front-line had been pushed back beyond its position before the summer offensive. In mid-February, after the Soviet push had tapered off, the Germans launched another <a href="/wiki/Third_Battle_of_Kharkov" title="Third Battle of Kharkov">attack on Kharkov</a>, creating a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salients,_re-entrants_and_pockets" title="Salients, re-entrants and pockets">salient</a> in their front line around the Russian city of <a href="/wiki/Kursk" title="Kursk">Kursk</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEErickson2001142_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEErickson2001142-200">[198]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span id="Western_Europe/Atlantic_&amp;_Mediterranean_(1942–43)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_Europe.2FAtlantic_.26_Mediterranean_.281942.E2.80.9343.29">Western Europe/Atlantic &amp; Mediterranean (1942–43)</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:8th_AF_Bombing_Marienburg.JPEG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2187" data-file-width="2716" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/8th_AF_Bombing_Marienburg.JPEG/220px-8th_AF_Bombing_Marienburg.JPEG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/8th_AF_Bombing_Marienburg.JPEG/330px-8th_AF_Bombing_Marienburg.JPEG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/8th_AF_Bombing_Marienburg.JPEG/440px-8th_AF_Bombing_Marienburg.JPEG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:8th_AF_Bombing_Marienburg.JPEG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/8th_Air_Force" title="8th Air Force">8th Air Force</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_B-17_Flying_Fortress" title="Boeing B-17 Flying Fortress">Boeing B-17 Flying Fortress</a> bombing raid on the Focke-Wulf factory in Germany, 9 October 1943</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Exploiting poor American naval command decisions, <a href="/wiki/Second_Happy_Time" title="Second Happy Time">the German navy ravaged Allied shipping off the American Atlantic coast</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMilner199052_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMilner199052-201">[199]</a></sup> By November 1941, Commonwealth forces had launched a counter-offensive, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Crusader" title="Operation Crusader">Operation Crusader</a>, in North Africa, and reclaimed all the gains the Germans and Italians had made.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012224.E2.80.938_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012224.E2.80.938-202">[200]</a></sup> In North Africa, the Germans launched an offensive in January, pushing the British back to positions at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gazala_Line" title="Gazala Line">Gazala Line</a> by early February,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMolinari200791_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMolinari200791-203">[201]</a></sup> followed by a temporary lull in combat which Germany used to prepare for their upcoming offensives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMitcham200731_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMitcham200731-204">[202]</a></sup> Concerns the Japanese might use bases in Vichy-held <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> caused the British to <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Madagascar" title="Battle of Madagascar">invade the island</a> in early May 1942.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012380.E2.80.931_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2012380.E2.80.931-205">[203]</a></sup> An Axis <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gazala" title="Battle of Gazala">offensive in Libya</a> forced an Allied retreat deep inside Egypt until Axis forces were <a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_El_Alamein" title="First Battle of El Alamein">stopped at El Alamein</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERich1992178_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERich1992178-206">[204]</a></sup> On the Continent, raids of Allied <a href="/wiki/Commando" title="Commando">commandos</a> on strategic targets, culminating in the disastrous <a href="/wiki/Dieppe_Raid" title="Dieppe Raid">Dieppe Raid</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGordon2004129_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon2004129-207">[205]</a></sup> demonstrated the Western Allies' inability to launch an invasion of continental Europe without much better preparation, equipment, and operational security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillands2005_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillands2005-208">[206]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2016)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In August 1942, the Allies succeeded in repelling a <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Alam_el_Halfa" title="Battle of Alam el Halfa">second attack against El Alamein</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeegan1997277_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan1997277-209">[207]</a></sup> and, at a high cost, managed to <a href="/wiki/Operation_Pedestal" title="Operation Pedestal">deliver desperately needed supplies to the besieged Malta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2002_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2002-210">[208]</a></sup> A few months later, the Allies <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_El_Alamein" title="Second Battle of El Alamein">commenced an attack of their own</a> in Egypt, dislodging the Axis forces and beginning a drive west across Libya.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomasAndrew19988_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomasAndrew19988-211">[209]</a></sup> This attack was followed up shortly after by <a href="/wiki/Operation_Torch" title="Operation Torch">Anglo-American landings in French North Africa</a>, which resulted in the region joining the Allies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoss199738_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoss199738-212">[210]</a></sup> Hitler responded to the French colony's defection by ordering the <a href="/wiki/Case_Anton" title="Case Anton">occupation of Vichy France</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoss199738_212-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoss199738-212">[210]</a></sup> although Vichy forces did not resist this violation of the armistice, they managed to <a href="/wiki/Scuttling_of_the_French_fleet_in_Toulon" title="Scuttling of the French fleet in Toulon">scuttle their fleet</a> to prevent its capture by German forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoss199738_212-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoss199738-212">[210]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBonnerBonner200124_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBonnerBonner200124-213">[211]</a></sup> The now pincered Axis forces in Africa withdrew into <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>, which was <a href="/wiki/Tunisian_Campaign" title="Tunisian Campaign">conquered by the Allies</a> in May 1943.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoss199738_212-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoss199738-212">[210]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollier200311_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollier200311-214">[212]</a></sup></p>
<p>In early 1943 the British and Americans began the <a href="/wiki/Combined_Bomber_Offensive" title="Combined Bomber Offensive">Combined Bomber Offensive</a>, a strategic bombing campaign against Germany. The goals were to disrupt the German war economy, reduce German morale, and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/De-housing" title="De-housing">de-house</a>" the civilian population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[213]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Allies_gain_momentum_(1943–44)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Allies_gain_momentum_.281943.E2.80.9344.29">Allies gain momentum (1943–44)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
