<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SBD_VB-16_over_USS_Washington_1943.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1658" data-file-width="2131" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/SBD_VB-16_over_USS_Washington_1943.jpg/220px-SBD_VB-16_over_USS_Washington_1943.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/SBD_VB-16_over_USS_Washington_1943.jpg/330px-SBD_VB-16_over_USS_Washington_1943.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/SBD_VB-16_over_USS_Washington_1943.jpg/440px-SBD_VB-16_over_USS_Washington_1943.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SBD_VB-16_over_USS_Washington_1943.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
US Navy <a href="/wiki/Douglas_SBD_Dauntless" title="Douglas SBD Dauntless">SBD-5</a> <a href="/wiki/Scout_plane" title="Scout plane">scout plane</a> flies patrol over <a href="/wiki/USS_Washington_(BB-56)" title="USS Washington (BB-56)">USS <i>Washington</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/USS_Lexington_(CV-2)" title="USS Lexington (CV-2)">USS <i>Lexington</i></a> during the Gilbert and Marshall Islands campaign, 1943</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the Guadalcanal Campaign, the Allies initiated several operations against Japan in the Pacific. In May 1943, Canadian and U.S. forces were sent to <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands_Campaign#Allied_response" title="Aleutian Islands Campaign">eliminate Japanese forces from the Aleutians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThompsonRandall2008164_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThompsonRandall2008164-216">[214]</a></sup> Soon after, the U.S., with support from Australian and New Zealand forces, began major operations to <a href="/wiki/Operation_Cartwheel" title="Operation Cartwheel">isolate Rabaul by capturing surrounding islands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_and_Marshall_Islands_campaign" title="Gilbert and Marshall Islands campaign">breach the Japanese Central Pacific perimeter at the Gilbert and Marshall Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2001610_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2001610-217">[215]</a></sup> By the end of March 1944, the Allies had completed both of these objectives, and had also <a href="/wiki/Operation_Hailstone" title="Operation Hailstone">neutralised the major Japanese base at Truk</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">Caroline Islands</a>. In April, the Allies launched an operation to <a href="/wiki/Western_New_Guinea_campaign" title="Western New Guinea campaign">retake Western New Guinea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERottman2002228_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERottman2002228-218">[216]</a></sup> In the Soviet Union, both the Germans and the Soviets spent the spring and early summer of 1943 preparing for large offensives in central Russia. On 4 July 1943, Germany <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kursk" title="Battle of Kursk">attacked Soviet forces around the Kursk Bulge</a>. Within a week, German forces had exhausted themselves against the Soviets' deeply echeloned and well-constructed defences<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[217]</a></sup> and, for the first time in the war, Hitler cancelled the operation before it had achieved tactical or operational success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2001592_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2001592-220">[218]</a></sup> This decision was partially affected by the Western Allies' <a href="/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Sicily" title="Allied invasion of Sicily">invasion of Sicily</a> launched on 9 July which, combined with previous Italian failures, resulted in the ousting and arrest of Mussolini later that month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEO.27Reilly200132_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO.27Reilly200132-221">[219]</a></sup> Also, in July 1943 the British <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Hamburg_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Hamburg in World War II">firebombed Hamburg</a> killing over 40,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOvery1995119.E2.80.93120_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOvery1995119.E2.80.93120-222">[220]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kursk_Soviet_machineguns.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="671" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Kursk_Soviet_machineguns.JPG/220px-Kursk_Soviet_machineguns.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Kursk_Soviet_machineguns.JPG/330px-Kursk_Soviet_machineguns.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Kursk_Soviet_machineguns.JPG/440px-Kursk_Soviet_machineguns.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kursk_Soviet_machineguns.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> troops, in a counter-offensive on German positions, at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kursk" title="Battle of Kursk">Battle of Kursk</a>, 1943</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 12 July 1943, the Soviets launched their own <a href="/wiki/Operation_Kutuzov" title="Operation Kutuzov">counter-offensives</a>, thereby dispelling any chance of German victory or even stalemate in the east. The Soviet victory at Kursk marked the end of German superiority,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBellamy2007595_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBellamy2007595-223">[221]</a></sup> giving the Soviet Union the initiative on the Eastern Front.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEO.27Reilly200135_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO.27Reilly200135-224">[222]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHealy199290_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHealy199290-225">[223]</a></sup> The Germans tried to stabilise their eastern front along the hastily fortified <a href="/wiki/Panther%E2%80%93Wotan_line" title="Panther–Wotan line">Panther–Wotan line</a>, but the Soviets broke through it at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Smolensk_(1943)" title="Battle of Smolensk (1943)">Smolensk</a> and by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lower_Dnieper_Offensive" title="Lower Dnieper Offensive">Lower Dnieper Offensives</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGlantz200150.E2.80.935_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGlantz200150.E2.80.935-226">[224]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 3 September 1943, the Western Allies <a href="/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Italy" title="Allied invasion of Italy">invaded the Italian mainland</a>, following <a href="/wiki/Armistice_of_Cassibile" title="Armistice of Cassibile">Italy's armistice with the Allies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[225]</a></sup> Germany with the help of fascists responded by disarming Italian forces that were in many places without superior orders, seizing military control of Italian areas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMazower2008362_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMazower2008362-228">[226]</a></sup> and creating a series of defensive lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHartHartHughes2000151_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHartHartHughes2000151-229">[227]</a></sup> German special forces then <a href="/wiki/Gran_Sasso_raid" title="Gran Sasso raid">rescued Mussolini</a>, who then soon established a new client state in German-occupied Italy named the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Social_Republic" title="Italian Social Republic">Italian Social Republic</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlinkhorn200652_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlinkhorn200652-230">[228]</a></sup> causing an <a href="/wiki/Italian_Civil_War" title="Italian Civil War">Italian civil war</a>. The Western Allies fought through several lines until reaching the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Line" title="Winter Line">main German defensive line</a> in mid-November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReadFisher2002129_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReadFisher2002129-231">[229]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cairo_conference.jpg"><img alt="Three men, Chiang Kai-shek, Roosevelt and Churchill, sitting together elbow to elbow" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="442" data-file-width="580" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Cairo_conference.jpg/220px-Cairo_conference.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Cairo_conference.jpg/330px-Cairo_conference.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Cairo_conference.jpg/440px-Cairo_conference.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cairo_conference.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Allied leaders of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">Asian and Pacific Theatre</a>: Generalissimo <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> meeting at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cairo_Conference_(1943)" title="Cairo Conference (1943)">Cairo Conference</a>, 25 November 1943</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>German operations in the Atlantic also suffered. By <a href="/wiki/Black_May_(1943)" title="Black May (1943)">May 1943, as Allied counter-measures became increasingly effective</a>, the resulting sizeable German submarine losses forced a temporary halt of the German Atlantic naval campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[230]</a></sup> In November 1943, <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> and Winston Churchill met with <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a> <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Conference" title="Cairo Conference">in Cairo</a> and then with Joseph Stalin <a href="/wiki/Tehran_Conference" title="Tehran Conference">in Tehran</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kolko_1990_211.2C235.2C267_268_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kolko_1990_211.2C235.2C267_268-233">[231]</a></sup> The former conference determined the post-war return of Japanese territory<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Iriye_1981_154_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-Iriye_1981_154-234">[232]</a></sup> and the military planning for the <a href="/wiki/Burma_Campaign" title="Burma Campaign">Burma Campaign</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMitter2014286_235-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMitter2014286-235">[233]</a></sup> while the latter included agreement that the Western Allies would invade Europe in 1944 and that the Soviet Union would declare war on Japan within three months of Germany's defeat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-polley148_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-polley148-236">[234]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Battle_of_Cassino,_January-may_1944_C4363.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="508" data-file-width="765" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/The_Battle_of_Cassino%2C_January-may_1944_C4363.jpg/220px-The_Battle_of_Cassino%2C_January-may_1944_C4363.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/The_Battle_of_Cassino%2C_January-may_1944_C4363.jpg/330px-The_Battle_of_Cassino%2C_January-may_1944_C4363.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/The_Battle_of_Cassino%2C_January-may_1944_C4363.jpg/440px-The_Battle_of_Cassino%2C_January-may_1944_C4363.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Battle_of_Cassino,_January-may_1944_C4363.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ruins of the <a href="/wiki/Monte_Cassino" title="Monte Cassino">Benedictine</a> monastery, during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Monte_Cassino" title="Battle of Monte Cassino">Battle of Monte Cassino</a>; <a href="/wiki/Italian_Campaign_(World_War_II)" title="Italian Campaign (World War II)">Italian Campaign</a>, May 1944</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From November 1943, during the seven-week <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Changde" title="Battle of Changde">Battle of Changde</a>, the Chinese forced Japan to fight a costly war of attrition, while awaiting Allied relief.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beevor_2012_268_274_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beevor_2012_268_274-237">[235]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-H161_238-0"><a href="#cite_note-H161-238">[236]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hsu_Chang_412-416_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hsu_Chang_412-416-239">[237]</a></sup> In January 1944, the Allies launched a <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Monte_Cassino" title="Battle of Monte Cassino">series of attacks in Italy against the line at Monte Cassino</a> and tried to outflank it with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Shingle" title="Operation Shingle">landings at Anzio</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[238]</a></sup> By the end of January, a major <a href="/wiki/Leningrad_Front" title="Leningrad Front">Soviet</a> <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Leningrad#Soviet_relief_of_the_siege" title="Siege of Leningrad">offensive expelled German forces</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Leningrad_Oblast" title="Leningrad Oblast">Leningrad region</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Glantz_2002_327_366_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-Glantz_2002_327_366-241">[239]</a></sup> ending the longest and <a href="/wiki/List_of_battles_by_casualties#Sieges_and_urban_combat" title="List of battles by casualties">most lethal siege in history</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Leningrad%E2%80%93Novgorod_Offensive" title="Leningrad–Novgorod Offensive">following Soviet offensive</a> was <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Narva_(1944)" title="Battle of Narva (1944)">halted on the pre-war Estonian border</a> by the German <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_North" title="Army Group North">Army Group North</a> aided by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Estonia_by_Nazi_Germany#Estonians_in_German_Military_Units_in_1941.E2.80.931944" title="Occupation of Estonia by Nazi Germany">Estonians</a> hoping to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Estonian_Government_in_Exile#Failure_to_reestablish_independence" title="Estonian Government in Exile">re-establish national independence</a>. This delay slowed subsequent Soviet operations in the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Glantz_2002_367_414_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-Glantz_2002_367_414-242">[240]</a></sup> By late May 1944, the Soviets had <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Offensive" title="Crimean Offensive">liberated Crimea</a>, largely expelled Axis forces from Ukraine, and made <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Jassy-Kishinev_Offensive" title="First Jassy-Kishinev Offensive">incursions into Romania</a>, which were repulsed by the Axis troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chubarov_2001_122_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chubarov_2001_122-243">[241]</a></sup> The Allied offensives in Italy had succeeded and, at the expense of allowing several German divisions to retreat, on 4 June, Rome was captured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[242]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Allies had mixed success in mainland Asia. In March 1944, the Japanese launched the first of two invasions, <a href="/wiki/Operation_U-Go" title="Operation U-Go">an operation against British positions in Assam, India</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lightbody_2004_224_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lightbody_2004_224-245">[243]</a></sup> and soon besieged Commonwealth positions at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Imphal" title="Battle of Imphal">Imphal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kohima" title="Battle of Kohima">Kohima</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zeiler_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zeiler-246">[244]</a></sup> In May 1944, British forces mounted a counter-offensive that drove Japanese troops back to Burma,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zeiler_246-1"><a href="#cite_note-Zeiler-246">[244]</a></sup> and Chinese forces that had <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Northern_Burma_and_Western_Yunnan" title="Battle of Northern Burma and Western Yunnan">invaded northern Burma</a> in late 1943 <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Myitkyina" title="Siege of Myitkyina">besieged Japanese troops</a> in <a href="/wiki/Myitkyina" title="Myitkyina">Myitkyina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[245]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Operation_Ichi-Go" title="Operation Ichi-Go">second Japanese invasion</a> of China aimed to destroy China's main fighting forces, secure railways between Japanese-held territory and capture Allied airfields.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[246]</a></sup> By June, the Japanese had conquered the province of <a href="/wiki/Henan" title="Henan">Henan</a> and begun a <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Changsha_(1944)" title="Battle of Changsha (1944)">new attack on Changsha</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Hunan" title="Hunan">Hunan</a> province.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[247]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Allies_close_in_(1944)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Allies_close_in_.281944.29">Allies close in (1944)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Approaching_Omaha.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2147" data-file-width="3000" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Approaching_Omaha.jpg/220px-Approaching_Omaha.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Approaching_Omaha.jpg/330px-Approaching_Omaha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Approaching_Omaha.jpg/440px-Approaching_Omaha.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Approaching_Omaha.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
American troops approaching <a href="/wiki/Omaha_Beach" title="Omaha Beach">Omaha Beach</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Normandy" title="Invasion of Normandy">Invasion of Normandy</a> on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D-Day" title="D-Day">D-Day</a>, 6 June 1944</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 6 June 1944 (known as <a href="/wiki/Normandy_landings" title="Normandy landings">D-Day</a>), after three years of Soviet pressure,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rees406_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-rees406-250">[248]</a></sup> the Western Allies <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Normandy" title="Invasion of Normandy">invaded northern France</a>. After reassigning several Allied divisions from Italy, they also <a href="/wiki/Operation_Dragoon" title="Operation Dragoon">attacked southern France</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weinberg_2005_695_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weinberg_2005_695-251">[249]</a></sup> These landings were successful, and led to the defeat of the <a href="/wiki/Falaise_Pocket" title="Falaise Pocket">German Army units</a> in France. Paris was <a href="/wiki/Liberation_of_Paris" title="Liberation of Paris">liberated</a> by the <a href="/wiki/French_Resistance" title="French Resistance">local resistance</a> assisted by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_French_Forces" title="Free French Forces">Free French Forces</a>, both led by General <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a>, on 25 August<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[250]</a></sup> and the Western Allies continued to <a href="/wiki/Allied_advance_from_Paris_to_the_Rhine" title="Allied advance from Paris to the Rhine">push back German forces</a> in western Europe during the latter part of the year. An attempt to advance into northern Germany spearheaded by <a href="/wiki/Operation_Market_Garden" title="Operation Market Garden">a major airborne operation</a> in the Netherlands failed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[251]</a></sup> After that, the Western Allies slowly pushed into Germany, but <a href="/wiki/Operation_Queen" title="Operation Queen">failed to cross the Ruhr river</a> in a large offensive. In Italy, Allied advance also slowed due to the <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Line" title="Gothic Line">last major German defensive line</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[252]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-97906,_Warschauer_Aufstand,_Stra%C3%9Fenkampf.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="534" data-file-width="800" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-97906%2C_Warschauer_Aufstand%2C_Stra%C3%9Fenkampf.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-97906%2C_Warschauer_Aufstand%2C_Stra%C3%9Fenkampf.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-97906%2C_Warschauer_Aufstand%2C_Stra%C3%9Fenkampf.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-97906%2C_Warschauer_Aufstand%2C_Stra%C3%9Fenkampf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-97906%2C_Warschauer_Aufstand%2C_Stra%C3%9Fenkampf.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-97906%2C_Warschauer_Aufstand%2C_Stra%C3%9Fenkampf.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-97906,_Warschauer_Aufstand,_Stra%C3%9Fenkampf.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
German <a href="/wiki/Schutzstaffel" title="Schutzstaffel">SS</a> soldiers from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dirlewanger_Brigade" title="Dirlewanger Brigade">Dirlewanger Brigade</a>, tasked with suppressing the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising" title="Warsaw Uprising">Warsaw Uprising</a> against Nazi occupation, August 1944</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 22 June, the Soviets launched a strategic offensive in Belarus ("<a href="/wiki/Operation_Bagration" title="Operation Bagration">Operation Bagration</a>") that destroyed the German <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_Centre" title="Army Group Centre">Army Group Centre</a> almost completely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zaloga_1996_7_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zaloga_1996_7-255">[253]</a></sup> Soon after that <a href="/wiki/Lvov%E2%80%93Sandomierz_Offensive" title="Lvov–Sandomierz Offensive">another Soviet strategic offensive</a> forced German troops from Western Ukraine and Eastern Poland. The Soviet advance prompted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armia_Krajowa" title="Armia Krajowa">resistance forces in Poland</a> to <a href="/wiki/Operation_Tempest" title="Operation Tempest">initiate several uprisings</a> against the German occupation. However, the largest of these <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising" title="Warsaw Uprising">in Warsaw</a>, where German soldiers massacred 200,000 civilians, and a <a href="/wiki/Slovak_National_Uprising" title="Slovak National Uprising">national uprising</a> in <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Republic_(1939%E2%80%931945)" title="Slovak Republic (1939–1945)">Slovakia</a>, did not receive Soviet support and were subsequently suppressed by the Germans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[254]</a></sup> The Red Army's <a href="/wiki/Jassy%E2%80%93Kishinev_Offensive" title="Jassy–Kishinev Offensive">strategic offensive in eastern Romania</a> cut off and destroyed the <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_South_Ukraine" title="Army Group South Ukraine">considerable German troops there</a> and triggered <a href="/wiki/King_Michael%27s_Coup" title="King Michael's Coup">a successful coup d'état in Romania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_of_1944" title="Bulgarian coup d'état of 1944">in Bulgaria</a>, followed by those countries' shift to the Allied side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-countrystudies.us_257-0"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies.us-257">[255]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 1944, Soviet troops advanced into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Democratic_Federal_Yugoslavia" title="Democratic Federal Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> and forced the rapid withdrawal of German Army Groups <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_E" title="Army Group E">E</a> and <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_F" title="Army Group F">F</a> in <a href="/wiki/Axis_occupation_of_Greece" title="Axis occupation of Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albanian_Kingdom_(1943%E2%80%9344)" title="Albanian Kingdom (1943–44)">Albania</a> and Yugoslavia to rescue them from being cut off.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Evans_2008_653_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-Evans_2008_653-258">[256]</a></sup> By this point, the Communist-led <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Partisans" title="Yugoslav Partisans">Partisans</a> under Marshal <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Josip Broz Tito</a>, who had led an <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_in_Yugoslavia" title="World War II in Yugoslavia">increasingly successful guerrilla campaign</a> against the occupation since 1941, controlled much of the territory of Yugoslavia and engaged in delaying efforts against German forces further south. In northern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbia_(1941%E2%80%931944)" title="Serbia (1941–1944)">Serbia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a>, with limited support from Bulgarian forces, assisted the Partisans in a joint <a href="/wiki/Belgrade_Offensive" title="Belgrade Offensive">liberation of the capital city of Belgrade</a> on 20 October. A few days later, the Soviets launched a <a href="/wiki/Budapest_Offensive" title="Budapest Offensive">massive assault</a> against <a href="/wiki/Operation_Panzerfaust" title="Operation Panzerfaust">German-occupied</a> Hungary that lasted until <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Budapest" title="Battle of Budapest">the fall of Budapest</a> in February 1945.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[257]</a></sup> Unlike impressive Soviet victories in the Balkans, <a href="/wiki/Continuation_War" title="Continuation War">bitter Finnish resistance</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Vyborg%E2%80%93Petrozavodsk_Offensive" title="Vyborg–Petrozavodsk Offensive">Soviet offensive</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Karelian_Isthmus" title="Karelian Isthmus">Karelian Isthmus</a> denied the Soviets occupation of Finland and led to a <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Armistice" title="Moscow Armistice">Soviet-Finnish armistice</a> on relatively mild conditions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[258]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[259]</a></sup> although Finland was forced to <a href="/wiki/Lapland_War" title="Lapland War">fight their former allies</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1199" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg/220px-Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg/330px-Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg/440px-Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
General <a href="/wiki/Douglas_MacArthur" title="Douglas MacArthur">Douglas MacArthur</a> lands at <a href="/wiki/Leyte" title="Leyte">Leyte</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Leyte" title="Battle of Leyte">Battle of Leyte</a>, 20 October 1944</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By the start of July 1944, Commonwealth forces in Southeast Asia had repelled the Japanese sieges in Assam, pushing the Japanese back to the <a href="/wiki/Chindwin_River" title="Chindwin River">Chindwin River</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marston_2005_120_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marston_2005_120-262">[260]</a></sup> while the Chinese captured Myitkyina. In September 1944, Chinese force <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mount_Song" title="Battle of Mount Song">captured the Mount Song</a> to reopen the <a href="/wiki/Burma_Road" title="Burma Road">Burma Road</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[261]</a></sup> In China, the Japanese had more successes, having finally captured Changsha in mid-June and the city of <a href="/wiki/Defense_of_Hengyang" title="Defense of Hengyang">Hengyang</a> by early August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[262]</a></sup> Soon after, they invaded the province of Guangxi, winning major engagements against Chinese forces at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guilin%E2%80%93Liuzhou" title="Battle of Guilin–Liuzhou">Guilin and Liuzhou</a> by the end of November<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[263]</a></sup> and successfully linking up their forces in China and Indochina by mid-December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drea_2003_54_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-Drea_2003_54-266">[264]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the Pacific, US forces continued to press back the Japanese perimeter. In mid-June 1944, they began their <a href="/wiki/Mariana_and_Palau_Islands_campaign" title="Mariana and Palau Islands campaign">offensive against the Mariana and Palau islands</a>, and decisively defeated Japanese forces in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Philippine_Sea" title="Battle of the Philippine Sea">Battle of the Philippine Sea</a>. These defeats led to the resignation of the Japanese Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Hideki_Tojo" title="Hideki Tojo">Hideki Tojo</a>, and provided the United States with air bases to launch intensive heavy bomber attacks on the Japanese home islands. In late October, American forces <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Leyte" title="Battle of Leyte">invaded the Filipino island of Leyte</a>; soon after, Allied naval forces scored another large victory in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Leyte_Gulf" title="Battle of Leyte Gulf">Battle of Leyte Gulf</a>, one of the largest naval battles in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[265]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Axis_collapse,_Allied_victory_(1944–45)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Axis_collapse.2C_Allied_victory_.281944.E2.80.9345.29">Axis collapse, Allied victory (1944–45)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yalta_Conference_(Churchill,_Roosevelt,_Stalin)_(B%26W).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2239" data-file-width="2720" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg/220px-Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg/330px-Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg/440px-Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yalta_Conference_(Churchill,_Roosevelt,_Stalin)_(B%26W).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a> held in February 1945, with <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 16 December 1944, Germany made a last attempt on the Western Front by using most of its remaining reserves to launch <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Bulge" title="Battle of the Bulge">a massive counter-offensive in the Ardennes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Nordwind" title="Operation Nordwind">along the French–German border</a> to split the Western Allies, encircle large portions of Western Allied troops and capture their primary supply port at <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> to prompt a political settlement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parkerxiii_268-0"><a href="#cite_note-parkerxiii-268">[266]</a></sup> By January, the offensive had been repulsed with no strategic objectives fulfilled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parkerxiii_268-1"><a href="#cite_note-parkerxiii-268">[266]</a></sup> In Italy, the Western Allies remained stalemated at the German defensive line. In mid-January 1945, the Soviets and Poles attacked in Poland, <a href="/wiki/Vistula%E2%80%93Oder_Offensive" title="Vistula–Oder Offensive">pushing from the Vistula to the Oder</a> river in Germany, and <a href="/wiki/East_Prussian_Offensive" title="East Prussian Offensive">overran East Prussia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[267]</a></sup> On 4 February, Soviet, British and US leaders met for the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a>. They agreed on the occupation of post-war Germany, and on when the Soviet Union would join the war against Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[268]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February, the Soviets <a href="/wiki/Silesian_Offensives" title="Silesian Offensives">entered Silesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Pomeranian_Offensive" title="East Pomeranian Offensive">Pomerania</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Western_Allied_invasion_of_Germany" title="Western Allied invasion of Germany">Western Allies entered western Germany</a> and closed to the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> river. By March, the Western Allies crossed the Rhine <a href="/wiki/Operation_Plunder" title="Operation Plunder">north</a> and <a href="/wiki/Remagen" title="Remagen">south</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Ruhr" title="Rhine-Ruhr">Ruhr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_Pocket" title="Ruhr Pocket">encircling the German Army Group B</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[269]</a></sup> while the Soviets advanced to <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>. In early April, the Western Allies finally <a href="/wiki/Spring_1945_offensive_in_Italy" title="Spring 1945 offensive in Italy">pushed forward in Italy</a> and swept across western Germany capturing <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hamburg_(1945)" title="Battle of Hamburg (1945)">Hamburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nuremberg_(1945)" title="Battle of Nuremberg (1945)">Nuremberg</a>, while Soviet and Polish forces <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Berlin" title="Battle of Berlin">stormed Berlin</a> in late April. <a href="/wiki/Elbe_Day" title="Elbe Day">American and Soviet forces met at the Elbe river</a> on 25 April. On 30 April 1945, the <a href="/wiki/Reichstag_building" title="Reichstag building">Reichstag</a> was captured, signalling the military defeat of Nazi Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shepardson_1998_272-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shepardson_1998-272">[270]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several changes in leadership occurred during this period. On 12 April, President Roosevelt died and was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">Harry S. Truman</a>. Benito Mussolini <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Benito_Mussolini" title="Death of Benito Mussolini">was killed</a> by <a href="/wiki/Italian_resistance_movement" title="Italian resistance movement">Italian partisans</a> on 28 April.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O.27Reilly_2001_244_273-0"><a href="#cite_note-O.27Reilly_2001_244-273">[271]</a></sup> Two days later, <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Adolf_Hitler" title="Death of Adolf Hitler">Hitler committed suicide</a>, and was succeeded by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Admiral" title="Grand Admiral">Grand Admiral</a> <a href="/wiki/Karl_D%C3%B6nitz" title="Karl Dönitz">Karl Dönitz</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[272]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reichstag_after_the_allied_bombing_of_Berlin.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="764" height="230" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Reichstag_after_the_allied_bombing_of_Berlin.jpg/220px-Reichstag_after_the_allied_bombing_of_Berlin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Reichstag_after_the_allied_bombing_of_Berlin.jpg/330px-Reichstag_after_the_allied_bombing_of_Berlin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Reichstag_after_the_allied_bombing_of_Berlin.jpg/440px-Reichstag_after_the_allied_bombing_of_Berlin.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reichstag_after_the_allied_bombing_of_Berlin.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The German <a href="/wiki/Reichstag_building" title="Reichstag building">Reichstag</a> after its capture by the Allied forces, 3 June 1945</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>German forces surrendered in Italy on 29 April. <a href="/wiki/German_Instrument_of_Surrender" title="German Instrument of Surrender">Total and unconditional surrender</a> was signed <a href="/wiki/Victory_in_Europe_Day" title="Victory in Europe Day">on 7 May</a>, to be effective by the end of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Victory_Day_(Eastern_Front)" title="Victory Day (Eastern Front)">8 May</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Evans_2008_737_275-0"><a href="#cite_note-Evans_2008_737-275">[273]</a></sup> German Army Group Centre <a href="/wiki/Prague_Offensive" title="Prague Offensive">resisted in Prague</a> until 11 May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Glantz_1998_34_276-0"><a href="#cite_note-Glantz_1998_34-276">[274]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the Pacific theatre, American forces accompanied by the forces of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Commonwealth" title="Philippine Commonwealth">Philippine Commonwealth</a> advanced <a href="/wiki/Philippines_Campaign_(1944%E2%80%931945)" title="Philippines Campaign (1944–1945)">in the Philippines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Leyte" title="Battle of Leyte">clearing Leyte</a> by the end of April 1945. They <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Luzon" title="Battle of Luzon">landed on Luzon</a> in January 1945 and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_(1945)" title="Battle of Manila (1945)">recaptured Manila</a> in March following a battle which reduced the city to ruins. Fighting continued on Luzon, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mindanao" title="Battle of Mindanao">Mindanao</a>, and other islands of the Philippines until the <a href="/wiki/End_of_World_War_II_in_Asia" title="End of World War II in Asia">end of the war</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[275]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Air_Forces" title="United States Army Air Forces">United States Army Air Forces</a> (USAAF) were destroying strategic and populated cities and towns in Japan in an effort to destroy Japanese war industry and civilian morale. On the night of 9–10 March, USAAF <a href="/wiki/Boeing_B-29_Superfortress" title="Boeing B-29 Superfortress">B-29</a> <a href="/wiki/Bomber" title="Bomber">bombers</a> <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Tokyo" title="Bombing of Tokyo">struck Tokyo</a> with thousands of <a href="/wiki/Incendiary_device" title="Incendiary device">incendiary bombs</a>, which killed 100,000 civilians and destroyed 16 square miles (41 km<sup>2</sup>) within a few hours. Over the next five months, the USAAF <a href="/wiki/Air_raids_on_Japan" title="Air raids on Japan">firebombed a total of 67 Japanese cities</a>, killing 393,000 civilians and destroying 65% of built-up areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[276]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 1945, Australian troops <a href="/wiki/Borneo_campaign_(1945)" title="Borneo campaign (1945)">landed in Borneo</a>, overrunning the oilfields there. British, American, and Chinese forces defeated the Japanese in northern <a href="/wiki/Burma_Campaign" title="Burma Campaign">Burma</a> in March, and the British pushed on to reach <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rangoon" title="Rangoon">Rangoon</a> by 3 May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drea_2003_57_279-0"><a href="#cite_note-Drea_2003_57-279">[277]</a></sup> Chinese forces started to counterattack in <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_West_Hunan" title="Battle of West Hunan">Battle of West Hunan</a> that occurred between 6 April and 7 June 1945. American naval and amphibious forces also moved towards Japan, taking <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Iwo_Jima" title="Battle of Iwo Jima">Iwo Jima</a> by March, and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Okinawa" title="Battle of Okinawa">Okinawa</a> by the end of June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[278]</a></sup> At the same time, American submarines <a href="/wiki/Allied_submarines_in_the_Pacific_War" title="Allied submarines in the Pacific War">cut off</a> Japanese imports, drastically reducing Japan's ability to supply its overseas forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-results_of_german_and_american_submarines_281-0"><a href="#cite_note-results_of_german_and_american_submarines-281">[279]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shigemitsu-signs-surrender.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="593" data-file-width="740" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Shigemitsu-signs-surrender.jpg/220px-Shigemitsu-signs-surrender.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Shigemitsu-signs-surrender.jpg/330px-Shigemitsu-signs-surrender.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Shigemitsu-signs-surrender.jpg/440px-Shigemitsu-signs-surrender.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shigemitsu-signs-surrender.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Japanese foreign affairs minister <a href="/wiki/Mamoru_Shigemitsu" title="Mamoru Shigemitsu">Mamoru Shigemitsu</a> signs the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Instrument_of_Surrender" title="Japanese Instrument of Surrender">Japanese Instrument of Surrender</a> on board <a href="/wiki/USS_Missouri_(BB-63)" title="USS Missouri (BB-63)">USS <i>Missouri</i></a>, 2 September 1945</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 11 July, Allied leaders <a href="/wiki/Potsdam_Conference" title="Potsdam Conference">met in Potsdam, Germany</a>. They <a href="/wiki/Potsdam_Agreement" title="Potsdam Agreement">confirmed earlier agreements</a> about Germany,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_2006_90_282-0"><a href="#cite_note-Williams_2006_90-282">[280]</a></sup> and reiterated the demand for unconditional surrender of all Japanese forces by Japan, specifically stating that "the alternative for Japan is prompt and utter destruction".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miscamble_2007_201_283-0"><a href="#cite_note-Miscamble_2007_201-283">[281]</a></sup> During this conference, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1945" title="United Kingdom general election, 1945">United Kingdom held its general election</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Clement_Attlee" title="Clement Attlee">Clement Attlee</a> replaced Churchill as Prime Minister.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miscamble_2007_203_204_284-0"><a href="#cite_note-Miscamble_2007_203_204-284">[282]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Allies called for unconditional Japanese surrender in the <a href="/wiki/Potsdam_Declaration" title="Potsdam Declaration">Potsdam Declaration</a> of 27 July, but the Japanese government rejected the call. In early August, the USAAF <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">dropped atomic bombs</a> on the Japanese cities of <a href="/wiki/Hiroshima" title="Hiroshima">Hiroshima</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nagasaki" title="Nagasaki">Nagasaki</a>. The Allies justified the atomic bombings as a military necessity to avoid <a href="/wiki/Operation_Downfall" title="Operation Downfall">invading the Japanese home islands</a> which would cost the lives of between 250,000 and 500,000 Allied servicemen and millions of Japanese troops and civilians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[283]</a></sup> Between the two bombings, the Soviets, pursuant to the Yalta agreement, <a href="/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria" title="Soviet invasion of Manchuria">invaded Japanese-held Manchuria</a>, and quickly defeated the <a href="/wiki/Kwantung_Army" title="Kwantung Army">Kwantung Army</a>, which was the largest Japanese fighting force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[284]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pape_1993_287-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pape_1993-287">[285]</a></sup> The Red Army also captured <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin" title="Sakhalin">Sakhalin</a> Island and the <a href="/wiki/Kuril_Islands" title="Kuril Islands">Kuril Islands</a>. On 15 August 1945, <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">Japan surrendered</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Instrument_of_Surrender" title="Japanese Instrument of Surrender">surrender documents</a> finally signed at <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Bay" title="Tokyo Bay">Tokyo Bay</a> on the deck of the American battleship <a href="/wiki/USS_Missouri_(BB-63)" title="USS Missouri (BB-63)">USS <i>Missouri</i></a> on 2 September 1945, ending the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beevor_2012_776_288-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beevor_2012_776-288">[286]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_II" title="Aftermath of World War II">Aftermath of World War II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Consequences_of_Nazism" title="Consequences of Nazism">Consequences of Nazism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ww2_170.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2404" data-file-width="2951" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Ww2_170.jpg/220px-Ww2_170.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Ww2_170.jpg/330px-Ww2_170.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Ww2_170.jpg/440px-Ww2_170.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ww2_170.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Defendants at the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_trials" title="Nuremberg trials">Nuremberg trials</a>, where the Allied forces prosecuted prominent members of the political, military, judicial and economic leadership of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> for <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Allies established occupation administrations in <a href="/wiki/Allied-occupied_Austria" title="Allied-occupied Austria">Austria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Allied-occupied_Germany" title="Allied-occupied Germany">Germany</a>. The former became a neutral state, non-aligned with any political bloc. The latter was divided into western and eastern occupation zones controlled by the Western Allies and the USSR, accordingly. A <a href="/wiki/Denazification" title="Denazification">denazification</a> programme in Germany led to the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_trials" title="Nuremberg trials">prosecution of Nazi war criminals</a> and the removal of ex-Nazis from power, although this policy moved towards amnesty and re-integration of ex-Nazis into West German society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frei_2002_41_66_289-0"><a href="#cite_note-Frei_2002_41_66-289">[287]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Destroyed_Warsaw,_capital_of_Poland,_January_1945.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="824" data-file-width="1000" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Destroyed_Warsaw%2C_capital_of_Poland%2C_January_1945.jpg/220px-Destroyed_Warsaw%2C_capital_of_Poland%2C_January_1945.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Destroyed_Warsaw%2C_capital_of_Poland%2C_January_1945.jpg/330px-Destroyed_Warsaw%2C_capital_of_Poland%2C_January_1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Destroyed_Warsaw%2C_capital_of_Poland%2C_January_1945.jpg/440px-Destroyed_Warsaw%2C_capital_of_Poland%2C_January_1945.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Destroyed_Warsaw,_capital_of_Poland,_January_1945.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ruins of <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a> in January 1945, after the <a href="/wiki/Planned_destruction_of_Warsaw" title="Planned destruction of Warsaw">deliberate destruction of the city</a> by the occupying German forces</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Germany lost a quarter of its pre-war (1937) territory. Among the eastern territories, <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neumark" title="Neumark">Neumark</a> and most of <a href="/wiki/Pomerania" title="Pomerania">Pomerania</a> were taken over by Poland, <a href="/wiki/East_Prussia" title="East Prussia">East Prussia</a> was divided between Poland and the USSR, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Flight_and_expulsion_of_Germans_(1944%E2%80%9350)" title="Flight and expulsion of Germans (1944–50)">expulsion of the 9 million Germans</a> from these provinces, as well as the expulsion of 3 million Germans from the <a href="/wiki/Sudetenland" title="Sudetenland">Sudetenland</a> in Czechoslovakia to Germany. By the 1950s, every fifth West German was a refugee from the east. The Soviet Union also took over the Polish provinces east of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Curzon_line" title="Curzon line">Curzon line</a>, from which <a href="/wiki/Polish_population_transfers_(1944%E2%80%931946)" title="Polish population transfers (1944–1946)">2 million Poles were expelled</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stalinswars43_290-0"><a href="#cite_note-stalinswars43-290">[288]</a></sup> north-east Romania,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stalinswars55_291-0"><a href="#cite_note-stalinswars55-291">[289]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shirer794_292-0"><a href="#cite_note-shirer794-292">[290]</a></sup> parts of eastern Finland,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ckpipe_293-0"><a href="#cite_note-ckpipe-293">[291]</a></sup> and the three <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a> were also <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_the_Baltic_states_(1944)" title="Soviet occupation of the Baltic states (1944)">incorporated into the USSR</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wettig_2008_20_21_294-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wettig_2008_20_21-294">[292]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Senn_2007_.3F_295-0"><a href="#cite_note-Senn_2007_.3F-295">[293]</a></sup></p>
<p>In an effort to maintain <a href="/wiki/World_peace" title="World peace">world peace</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yoder_1997_39_296-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yoder_1997_39-296">[294]</a></sup> the Allies formed the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, which officially came into existence on 24 October 1945,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297"><a href="#cite_note-297">[295]</a></sup> and adopted the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a> in 1948, as a common standard for all <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">member nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Waltz_2002_298-0"><a href="#cite_note-Waltz_2002-298">[296]</a></sup> The great powers that were the victors of the war—France, China, Britain, the Soviet Union and the United States—became the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council" title="Permanent members of the United Nations Security Council">permanent members</a> of the UN's <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_UN_Security_Council_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_UN_Security_Council-9">[7]</a></sup> The five permanent members remain so to the present, although there have been two seat changes, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_2758" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 2758">between</a> the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Republic of China</a> and the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a> in 1971, and between the Soviet Union and its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Successor_state" title="Successor state">successor state</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian Federation</a>, following the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> in 1991. The alliance between the Western Allies and the Soviet Union had begun to deteriorate even before the war was over.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kantowicz_2000_6_299-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kantowicz_2000_6-299">[297]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EasternBloc_BorderChange38-48.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="643" data-file-width="396" height="292" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/EasternBloc_BorderChange38-48.svg/180px-EasternBloc_BorderChange38-48.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/EasternBloc_BorderChange38-48.svg/270px-EasternBloc_BorderChange38-48.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/EasternBloc_BorderChange38-48.svg/360px-EasternBloc_BorderChange38-48.svg.png 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EasternBloc_BorderChange38-48.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Post-war Soviet territorial expansion resulted in <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern European</a> border changes, the creation of a <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Communist Bloc</a> and start of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Germany had been <i>de facto</i> divided, and two independent states, the <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">Federal Republic of Germany</a> and the <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">German Democratic Republic</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wettig_2008_96_100_300-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wettig_2008_96_100-300">[298]</a></sup> were created within the borders of <a href="/wiki/Bizone" title="Bizone">Allied</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_zone" title="Soviet occupation zone">Soviet occupation zones</a>, accordingly. The rest of Europe was also divided into Western and Soviet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spheres_of_influence" title="Spheres of influence">spheres of influence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trachtenberg_1999_33_301-0"><a href="#cite_note-Trachtenberg_1999_33-301">[299]</a></sup> Most eastern and central European countries fell into <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">the Soviet sphere</a>, which led to establishment of Communist-led regimes, with full or partial support of the Soviet occupation authorities. As a result, <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Applebaum_2012_302-0"><a href="#cite_note-Applebaum_2012-302">[300]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Polish_People%27s_Republic" title="Polish People's Republic">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_People%27s_Republic" title="Hungarian People's Republic">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Romania" title="Socialist Republic of Romania">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovak_Socialist_Republic" title="Czechoslovak Socialist Republic">Czechoslovakia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Socialist_Republic_of_Albania" title="People's Socialist Republic of Albania">Albania</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Naimark_2010_303-0"><a href="#cite_note-Naimark_2010-303">[301]</a></sup> became Soviet <a href="/wiki/Satellite_state" title="Satellite state">satellite states</a>. Communist <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> conducted a fully <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">independent policy</a>, causing <a href="/wiki/Tito%E2%80%93Stalin_Split" title="Tito–Stalin Split">tension with the USSR</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Swain_1992_304-0"><a href="#cite_note-Swain_1992-304">[302]</a></sup></p>
<p>Post-war division of the world was formalised by two international military alliances, the United States-led <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> and the Soviet-led <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Borstelmann_2005_318_305-0"><a href="#cite_note-Borstelmann_2005_318-305">[303]</a></sup> the long period of political tensions and military competition between them, the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, would be accompanied by an unprecedented <a href="/wiki/Arms_race" title="Arms race">arms race</a> and <a href="/wiki/Proxy_war" title="Proxy war">proxy wars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-306"><a href="#cite_note-306">[304]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Asia, the United States led the <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Japan" title="Occupation of Japan">occupation of Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trust_Territory_of_the_Pacific_Islands" title="Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands">administrated Japan's former islands in the Western Pacific</a>, while the Soviets annexed <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin" title="Sakhalin">Sakhalin</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kuril_Islands" title="Kuril Islands">Kuril Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weinberg_2005_911_307-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weinberg_2005_911-307">[305]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a>, formerly <a href="/wiki/Korea_under_Japanese_rule" title="Korea under Japanese rule">under Japanese rule</a>, was <a href="/wiki/Division_of_Korea" title="Division of Korea">divided and occupied</a> by the Soviet Union in the <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North</a> and the US in the <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South</a> between 1945 and 1948. Separate republics emerged on both sides of the 38th parallel in 1948, each claiming to be the legitimate government for all of Korea, which led ultimately to the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308">[306]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Declaration_of_State_of_Israel_1948.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="872" data-file-width="1280" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Declaration_of_State_of_Israel_1948.jpg/220px-Declaration_of_State_of_Israel_1948.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Declaration_of_State_of_Israel_1948.jpg/330px-Declaration_of_State_of_Israel_1948.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Declaration_of_State_of_Israel_1948.jpg/440px-Declaration_of_State_of_Israel_1948.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Declaration_of_State_of_Israel_1948.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion" title="David Ben-Gurion">David Ben-Gurion</a> proclaiming the <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Israeli Declaration of Independence">Israeli Declaration of Independence</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Independence_Hall_(Israel)" title="Independence Hall (Israel)">Independence Hall</a>, 14 May 1948</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In China, nationalist and communist forces resumed <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">the civil war</a> in June 1946. Communist forces were victorious and established the People's Republic of China on the mainland, while nationalist forces retreated to <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> in 1949.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lynch_2010_12_13_309-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lynch_2010_12_13-309">[307]</a></sup> In the Middle East, the Arab rejection of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine" title="United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine">United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Creation_of_Israel" title="Creation of Israel">creation of Israel</a> marked the escalation of the <a href="/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict" title="Arab–Israeli conflict">Arab–Israeli conflict</a>. While European powers attempted to retain some or all of their <a href="/wiki/Colonial_empire" title="Colonial empire">colonial empires</a>, their losses of prestige and resources during the war rendered this unsuccessful, leading to <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">decolonisation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMRoberts_1996_589_310-0"><a href="#cite_note-JMRoberts_1996_589-310">[308]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311">[309]</a></sup></p>
<p>The global economy suffered heavily from the war, although participating nations were affected differently. The US emerged much richer than any other nation; it had a <a href="/wiki/Post%E2%80%93World_War_II_baby_boom" title="Post–World War II baby boom">baby boom</a> and by 1950 its gross domestic product per person was much higher than that of any of the other powers and it dominated the world economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312"><a href="#cite_note-312">[310]</a></sup> The UK and US pursued a policy of <a href="/wiki/Allied_plans_for_German_industry_after_World_War_II" title="Allied plans for German industry after World War II">industrial disarmament in Western Germany</a> in the years 1945–1948.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Balabkins_1964_207_313-0"><a href="#cite_note-Balabkins_1964_207-313">[311]</a></sup> Because of international trade interdependencies this led to European economic stagnation and delayed European recovery for several years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-314"><a href="#cite_note-314">[312]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Balabkins_1964_208.2C209_315-0"><a href="#cite_note-Balabkins_1964_208.2C209-315">[313]</a></sup></p>
<p>Recovery began with the mid-1948 <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Mark" title="Deutsche Mark">currency reform in Western Germany</a>, and was sped up by the liberalisation of European economic policy that the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">Marshall Plan</a> (1948–1951) both directly and indirectly caused.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316">[314]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Balabkins_1964_212_317-0"><a href="#cite_note-Balabkins_1964_212-317">[315]</a></sup> The post-1948 West German recovery has been called the <a href="/wiki/Wirtschaftswunder#West_Germany" title="Wirtschaftswunder">German economic miracle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318">[316]</a></sup> Italy also experienced an <a href="/wiki/Italian_economic_miracle" title="Italian economic miracle">economic boom</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319">[317]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Trente_Glorieuses" title="Trente Glorieuses">French economy rebounded</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320"><a href="#cite_note-320">[318]</a></sup> By contrast, the United Kingdom was in a state of economic ruin,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321">[319]</a></sup> and although it received a quarter of the total Marshall Plan assistance, more than any other European country,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-322"><a href="#cite_note-322">[320]</a></sup> continued relative economic decline for decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-323"><a href="#cite_note-323">[321]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Soviet Union, despite enormous human and material losses, also experienced rapid increase in production in the immediate post-war era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith_1993_32_324-0"><a href="#cite_note-Smith_1993_32-324">[322]</a></sup> Japan experienced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_post-war_economic_miracle" title="Japanese post-war economic miracle">incredibly rapid</a> economic growth, becoming one of the most powerful economies in the world by the 1980s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325"><a href="#cite_note-325">[323]</a></sup> China returned to its pre-war industrial production by 1952.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326"><a href="#cite_note-326">[324]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">Impact</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Casualties_and_war_crimes">Casualties and war crimes</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_casualties" title="World War II casualties">World War II casualties</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_crimes_during_World_War_II" title="War crimes during World War II">War crimes during World War II</a>, <a href="/wiki/War_crimes_in_occupied_Poland_during_World_War_II" title="War crimes in occupied Poland during World War II">War crimes in occupied Poland during World War II</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_war_crimes" title="German war crimes">German war crimes</a>, <a href="/wiki/War_crimes_of_the_Wehrmacht" title="War crimes of the Wehrmacht">War crimes of the Wehrmacht</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_war_crimes" title="Italian war crimes">Italian war crimes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_war_crimes" title="Japanese war crimes">Japanese war crimes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allied_war_crimes_during_World_War_II" title="Allied war crimes during World War II">Allied war crimes during World War II</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_war_crimes" title="Soviet war crimes">Soviet war crimes</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:427px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:World_War_II_Casualties2.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="830" height="277" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/World_War_II_Casualties2.svg/425px-World_War_II_Casualties2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/World_War_II_Casualties2.svg/638px-World_War_II_Casualties2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/World_War_II_Casualties2.svg/850px-World_War_II_Casualties2.svg.png 2x" width="425"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:World_War_II_Casualties2.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
World War II deaths</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Estimates for the total number of casualties in the war vary, because many deaths went unrecorded. Most suggest that some 60 million people died in the war, including about <a href="/wiki/Battle_casualties_of_World_War_II" title="Battle casualties of World War II">20 million military personnel</a> and 40 million civilians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWII:_C.26C_327-0"><a href="#cite_note-WWII:_C.26C-327">[325]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328"><a href="#cite_note-328">[326]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-329"><a href="#cite_note-329">[327]</a></sup> Many of the civilians died because of deliberate <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_massacres" title="List of massacres">massacres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II" title="Strategic bombing during World War II">mass-bombings</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infectious_disease" title="Infectious disease">disease</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Starvation" title="Starvation">starvation</a>.</p>
<p>The Soviet Union lost around 27 million people during the war,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-330"><a href="#cite_note-330">[328]</a></sup> including 8.7 million military and 19 million civilian deaths. The largest portion of military dead were 5.7 million ethnic <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>, followed by 1.3 million ethnic <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ell.26Mak_1994_331-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ell.26Mak_1994-331">[329]</a></sup> A quarter of the people in the Soviet Union were wounded or killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-332"><a href="#cite_note-332">[330]</a></sup> Germany sustained 5.3 million military losses, mostly on the Eastern Front and during the final battles in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herf_2003_333-0"><a href="#cite_note-Herf_2003-333">[331]</a></sup></p>
<p>Of the total number of deaths in World War II, approximately 85 per cent—mostly Soviet and Chinese—were on the Allied side and 15 per cent were on the Axis side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-334"><a href="#cite_note-334">[332]</a></sup> Many of these deaths were caused by war crimes <a href="/wiki/War_crimes_of_the_Wehrmacht" title="War crimes of the Wehrmacht">committed by German</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_war_crimes" title="Japanese war crimes">Japanese forces</a> in occupied territories. An estimated 11<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-335"><a href="#cite_note-335">[333]</a></sup> to 17 million<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Niewyk45_336-0"><a href="#cite_note-Niewyk45-336">[334]</a></sup> civilians died either as a direct or as an indirect result of Nazi racist policies, including <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a> of around 6 million Jews, half of whom were Polish citizens, along with a further minimum 1.9 million ethnic Poles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-337"><a href="#cite_note-337">[335]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-338"><a href="#cite_note-338">[336]</a></sup> Millions of other Slavs (including Russians, Ukrainians and Belarusians), <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Roma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_homosexuals_in_Nazi_Germany_and_the_Holocaust" title="Persecution of homosexuals in Nazi Germany and the Holocaust">homosexuals</a>, and other ethnic and minority groups were also killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-339"><a href="#cite_note-339">[337]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Niewyk45_336-1"><a href="#cite_note-Niewyk45-336">[334]</a></sup> Hundreds of thousands (varying estimates) of ethnic <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a>, along with gypsies and Jews, were murdered by the Axis-aligned Croatian <a href="/wiki/Usta%C5%A1e" title="Ustaše">Ustaše</a> in <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-340"><a href="#cite_note-340">[338]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Bleiburg_repatriations" title="Bleiburg repatriations">retribution-related killings</a> were committed just after the war ended.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chinese_civilians_to_be_buried_alive.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="391" data-file-width="450" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Chinese_civilians_to_be_buried_alive.jpg/220px-Chinese_civilians_to_be_buried_alive.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Chinese_civilians_to_be_buried_alive.jpg/330px-Chinese_civilians_to_be_buried_alive.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Chinese_civilians_to_be_buried_alive.jpg/440px-Chinese_civilians_to_be_buried_alive.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chinese_civilians_to_be_buried_alive.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Chinese civilians being buried alive by soldiers of the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army" title="Imperial Japanese Army">Imperial Japanese Army</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/Nanking_Massacre" title="Nanking Massacre">Nanking Massacre</a>, December 1937</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Asia and the Pacific, between 3 million and more than 10 million civilians, mostly Chinese (estimated at 7.5 million<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-341"><a href="#cite_note-341">[339]</a></sup>), were killed by the Japanese occupation forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-342"><a href="#cite_note-342">[340]</a></sup> The best-known Japanese atrocity was the <a href="/wiki/Nanking_Massacre" title="Nanking Massacre">Nanking Massacre</a>, in which fifty to three hundred thousand Chinese civilians were raped and murdered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-343"><a href="#cite_note-343">[341]</a></sup> Mitsuyoshi Himeta reported that 2.7 million casualties occurred during the <i><a href="/wiki/Three_Alls_Policy" title="Three Alls Policy">Sankō Sakusen</a></i>. General <a href="/wiki/Yasuji_Okamura" title="Yasuji Okamura">Yasuji Okamura</a> implemented the policy in Heipei and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shantung" title="Shantung">Shantung</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-344"><a href="#cite_note-344">[342]</a></sup></p>
<p>Axis forces employed <a href="/wiki/Biological_warfare" title="Biological warfare">biological</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chemical_warfare" title="Chemical warfare">chemical weapons</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army" title="Imperial Japanese Army">Imperial Japanese Army</a> used a variety of such weapons during its <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">invasion and occupation of China</a> (<i>see <a href="/wiki/Unit_731" title="Unit 731">Unit 731</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-345"><a href="#cite_note-345">[343]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-346"><a href="#cite_note-346">[344]</a></sup> and in <a href="/wiki/Battles_of_Khalkhin_Gol" title="Battles of Khalkhin Gol">early conflicts against the Soviets</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-347"><a href="#cite_note-347">[345]</a></sup> Both the Germans and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_human_experimentation_on_the_Chinese" title="Japanese human experimentation on the Chinese">Japanese tested</a> such weapons against civilians<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-348"><a href="#cite_note-348">[346]</a></sup> and, sometimes on <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_war" title="Prisoner of war">prisoners of war</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-349"><a href="#cite_note-349">[347]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Soviet Union was responsible for the <a href="/wiki/Katyn_massacre" title="Katyn massacre">Katyn massacre</a> of 22,000 Polish officers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-350"><a href="#cite_note-350">[348]</a></sup> and the imprisonment or execution of thousands of political prisoners by the <a href="/wiki/NKVD" title="NKVD">NKVD</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-351"><a href="#cite_note-351">[349]</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Baltic_states" title="Occupation of the Baltic states">Baltic states</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_Poland_annexed_by_the_Soviet_Union" title="Territories of Poland annexed by the Soviet Union">eastern Poland</a> annexed by the Red Army.</p>
<p>The mass-bombing of cities in Europe and Asia has often been called a war crime. However, no <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Positive_international_law" title="Positive international law">positive</a> or specific <a href="/wiki/Customary_international_law" title="Customary international law">customary</a> <a href="/wiki/International_humanitarian_law" title="International humanitarian law">international humanitarian law</a> with respect to <a href="/wiki/Aerial_warfare" title="Aerial warfare">aerial warfare</a> existed before or during World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-352"><a href="#cite_note-352">[350]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Genocide,_concentration_camps,_and_slave_labour"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Genocide.2C_concentration_camps.2C_and_slave_labour">Genocide, concentration camps, and slave labour</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">Genocide</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">The Holocaust</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps" title="Nazi concentration camps">Nazi concentration camps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Extermination_camp" title="Extermination camp">Extermination camp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forced_labour_under_German_rule_during_World_War_II" title="Forced labour under German rule during World War II">Forced labour under German rule during World War II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kidnapping_of_children_by_Nazi_Germany" title="Kidnapping of children by Nazi Germany">Kidnapping of children by Nazi Germany</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nazi_human_experimentation" title="Nazi human experimentation">Nazi human experimentation</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Liberation_of_Bergen-belsen_Concentration_Camp,_April_1945_BU4031.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="789" data-file-width="800" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/The_Liberation_of_Bergen-belsen_Concentration_Camp%2C_April_1945_BU4031.jpg/220px-The_Liberation_of_Bergen-belsen_Concentration_Camp%2C_April_1945_BU4031.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/The_Liberation_of_Bergen-belsen_Concentration_Camp%2C_April_1945_BU4031.jpg/330px-The_Liberation_of_Bergen-belsen_Concentration_Camp%2C_April_1945_BU4031.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/The_Liberation_of_Bergen-belsen_Concentration_Camp%2C_April_1945_BU4031.jpg/440px-The_Liberation_of_Bergen-belsen_Concentration_Camp%2C_April_1945_BU4031.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Liberation_of_Bergen-belsen_Concentration_Camp,_April_1945_BU4031.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
