<a href="/wiki/Schutzstaffel" title="Schutzstaffel">Schutzstaffel</a> (SS) female camp guards remove prisoners' bodies from lorries and carry them to a mass grave, inside the German <a href="/wiki/Bergen-Belsen_concentration_camp" title="Bergen-Belsen concentration camp">Bergen-Belsen concentration camp</a>, 1945</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The German government led by <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a> was responsible for <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>, the killing of approximately 6 million Jews, as well as 2.7 million ethnic <a href="/wiki/Nazi_crimes_against_the_Polish_nation" title="Nazi crimes against the Polish nation">Poles</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-353"><a href="#cite_note-353">[351]</a></sup> and 4 million others who were deemed "<a href="/wiki/Life_unworthy_of_life" title="Life unworthy of life">unworthy of life</a>" (including the <a href="/wiki/Disability" title="Disability">disabled</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mental_disorder" title="Mental disorder">mentally ill</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_mistreatment_of_Soviet_prisoners_of_war" title="German mistreatment of Soviet prisoners of war">Soviet prisoners of war</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homosexuals" title="Homosexuals">homosexuals</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freemasons" title="Freemasons">Freemasons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani</a>) as part of a programme of deliberate extermination. About 12 million, most of whom were <a href="/wiki/Ostarbeiter" title="Ostarbeiter">Eastern Europeans</a>, were employed in the German war economy as <a href="/wiki/Forced_labour_under_German_rule_during_World_War_II" title="Forced labour under German rule during World War II">forced labourers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-compensation_354-0"><a href="#cite_note-compensation-354">[352]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps" title="Nazi concentration camps">Nazi concentration camps</a>, the Soviet <a href="/wiki/Gulag" title="Gulag">gulags</a> (<a href="/wiki/Labor_camp" title="Labor camp">labour camps</a>) led to the death of citizens of occupied countries such as Poland, Lithuania, Latvia, and Estonia, as well as German <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_war" title="Prisoner of war">prisoners of war</a> (POWs) and even Soviet citizens who had been or were thought to be supporters of the Nazis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-355"><a href="#cite_note-355">[353]</a></sup> Sixty per cent of <a href="/wiki/German_mistreatment_of_Soviet_prisoners_of_war" title="German mistreatment of Soviet prisoners of war">Soviet POWs of the Germans</a> died during the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-356"><a href="#cite_note-356">[354]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Overy" title="Richard Overy">Richard Overy</a> gives the number of 5.7 million Soviet POWs. Of those, 57 per cent died or were killed, a total of 3.6 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overy_2004_568_569_357-0"><a href="#cite_note-Overy_2004_568_569-357">[355]</a></sup> Soviet ex-POWs and repatriated civilians were treated with great suspicion as potential Nazi collaborators, and some of them were sent to the Gulag upon being checked by the NKVD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-358"><a href="#cite_note-358">[356]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Czeslawa_Kwoka_-_Brasse.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="665" data-file-width="1500" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Czeslawa_Kwoka_-_Brasse.jpg/220px-Czeslawa_Kwoka_-_Brasse.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Czeslawa_Kwoka_-_Brasse.jpg/330px-Czeslawa_Kwoka_-_Brasse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Czeslawa_Kwoka_-_Brasse.jpg/440px-Czeslawa_Kwoka_-_Brasse.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Czeslawa_Kwoka_-_Brasse.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Prisoner identity photograph taken by the German <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS" title="SS">SS</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Czes%C5%82awa_Kwoka" title="Czesława Kwoka">Polish girl deported as forced labour</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Auschwitz" title="Auschwitz">Auschwitz</a>, December 1942</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Japanese <a href="/wiki/Prisoner-of-war_camp" title="Prisoner-of-war camp">prisoner-of-war camps</a>, many of which were used as labour camps, also had high death rates. The <a href="/wiki/International_Military_Tribunal_for_the_Far_East" title="International Military Tribunal for the Far East">International Military Tribunal for the Far East</a> found the death rate of Western prisoners was 27.1 per cent (for American POWs, 37 per cent),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-359"><a href="#cite_note-359">[357]</a></sup> seven times that of POWs under the Germans and Italians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-360"><a href="#cite_note-360">[358]</a></sup> While 37,583 prisoners from the UK, 28,500 from the Netherlands, and 14,473 from the United States were released after the <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">surrender of Japan</a>, the number of Chinese released was only 56.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-361"><a href="#cite_note-361">[359]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to historian Zhifen Ju, at least five million Chinese civilians from northern China and Manchukuo were enslaved between 1935 and 1941 by the <a href="/wiki/East_Asia_Development_Board" title="East Asia Development Board">East Asia Development Board</a>, or <i>Kōain</i>, for work in mines and war industries. After 1942, the number reached 10 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhifen2002_362-0"><a href="#cite_note-zhifen2002-362">[360]</a></sup> The US Library of Congress estimates that in <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>, between 4 and 10 million <i><a href="/wiki/R%C5%8Dmusha" title="Rōmusha">rōmusha</a></i> (Japanese: "manual labourers"), were forced to work by the Japanese military. About 270,000 of these Javanese labourers were sent to other Japanese-held areas in South East Asia, and only 52,000 were repatriated to Java.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indonesiaww2_363-0"><a href="#cite_note-indonesiaww2-363">[361]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 19 February 1942, Roosevelt signed <a href="/wiki/Executive_Order_9066" title="Executive Order 9066">Executive Order 9066</a>, interning about 100,000 Japanese living on the West Coast. Canada had a similar programme.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-364"><a href="#cite_note-364">[362]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-365"><a href="#cite_note-365">[363]</a></sup> In addition, 14,000 German and Italian citizens who had been assessed as being security risks were also interned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kennedy_2001_749_750_366-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kennedy_2001_749_750-366">[364]</a></sup></p>
<p>In accordance with the Allied agreement made at the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a> millions of POWs and civilians were used as <a href="/wiki/Foreign_forced_labor_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Foreign forced labor in the Soviet Union">forced labour by the Soviet Union</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-367"><a href="#cite_note-367">[365]</a></sup> In Hungary's case, <a href="/wiki/Forced_labor_of_Hungarians_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Forced labor of Hungarians in the Soviet Union">Hungarians were forced to work for the Soviet Union</a> until 1955.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-368"><a href="#cite_note-368">[366]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Occupation">Occupation</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/German-occupied_Europe" title="German-occupied Europe">German-occupied Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebensraum" title="Lebensraum">Lebensraum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Untermensch" title="Untermensch">Untermensch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Collaboration_with_the_Axis_Powers_during_World_War_II" title="Collaboration with the Axis Powers during World War II">Collaboration with the Axis Powers during World War II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Resistance_during_World_War_II" title="Resistance during World War II">Resistance during World War II</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nazi_plunder" title="Nazi plunder">Nazi plunder</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palmiry_before_execution.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="307" data-file-width="480" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Palmiry_before_execution.jpg/220px-Palmiry_before_execution.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Palmiry_before_execution.jpg/330px-Palmiry_before_execution.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Palmiry_before_execution.jpg/440px-Palmiry_before_execution.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palmiry_before_execution.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Polish civilians wearing blindfolds photographed just before <a href="/wiki/Palmiry_massacre" title="Palmiry massacre">their execution by German soldiers in Palmiry forest</a>, 1940</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Europe, occupation came under two forms. In Western, Northern, and Central Europe (France, Norway, Denmark, the Low Countries, and the <a href="/wiki/Protectorate_of_Bohemia_and_Moravia" title="Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia">annexed portions of Czechoslovakia</a>) Germany established economic policies through which it collected roughly 69.5 billion reichmarks (27.8 billion US Dollars) by the end of the war, this figure does not include the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_plunder" title="Nazi plunder">sizeable plunder</a> of industrial products, military equipment, raw materials and other goods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-369"><a href="#cite_note-369">[367]</a></sup> Thus, the income from occupied nations was over 40 per cent of the income Germany collected from taxation, a figure which increased to nearly 40 per cent of total German income as the war went on.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Milward_1979_138_370-0"><a href="#cite_note-Milward_1979_138-370">[368]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-031-2436-03A,_Russland,_Hinrichtung_von_Partisanen_retouched.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="497" data-file-width="794" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-031-2436-03A%2C_Russland%2C_Hinrichtung_von_Partisanen_retouched.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-031-2436-03A%2C_Russland%2C_Hinrichtung_von_Partisanen_retouched.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-031-2436-03A%2C_Russland%2C_Hinrichtung_von_Partisanen_retouched.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-031-2436-03A%2C_Russland%2C_Hinrichtung_von_Partisanen_retouched.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-031-2436-03A%2C_Russland%2C_Hinrichtung_von_Partisanen_retouched.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-031-2436-03A%2C_Russland%2C_Hinrichtung_von_Partisanen_retouched.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-031-2436-03A,_Russland,_Hinrichtung_von_Partisanen_retouched.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Russian Academy of Sciences">Russian Academy of Sciences</a> reported in 1995 <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_casualties_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="World War II casualties of the Soviet Union">civilian victims in the Soviet Union</a> at German hands totalled 13.7 million dead, twenty percent of the 68 million persons in the occupied USSR</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the East, the intended gains of <i><a href="/wiki/Lebensraum" title="Lebensraum">Lebensraum</a></i> were never attained as fluctuating front-lines and Soviet <a href="/wiki/Scorched_earth" title="Scorched earth">scorched earth</a> policies denied resources to the German invaders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Milward_1992_148_371-0"><a href="#cite_note-Milward_1992_148-371">[369]</a></sup> Unlike in the West, the <a href="/wiki/Racial_policy_of_Nazi_Germany" title="Racial policy of Nazi Germany">Nazi racial policy</a> encouraged extreme brutality against what it considered to be the "<a href="/wiki/Untermensch" title="Untermensch">inferior people</a>" of Slavic descent; most German advances were thus followed by <a href="/wiki/Generalplan_Ost" title="Generalplan Ost">mass executions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-372"><a href="#cite_note-372">[370]</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/Resistance_during_World_War_II" title="Resistance during World War II">resistance groups</a> formed in most occupied territories, they did not significantly hamper German operations in either the East<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-373"><a href="#cite_note-373">[371]</a></sup> or the West<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-374"><a href="#cite_note-374">[372]</a></sup> until late 1943.</p>
<p>In Asia, Japan termed nations under its occupation as being part of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_East_Asia_Co-Prosperity_Sphere" title="Greater East Asia Co-Prosperity Sphere">Greater East Asia Co-Prosperity Sphere</a>, essentially a Japanese <a href="/wiki/Hegemony" title="Hegemony">hegemony</a> which it claimed was for purposes of liberating colonised peoples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-375"><a href="#cite_note-375">[373]</a></sup> Although Japanese forces were originally welcomed as liberators from European domination in some territories, their excessive brutality turned local public opinion against them within weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GSWW6_266_376-0"><a href="#cite_note-GSWW6_266-376">[374]</a></sup> During Japan's initial conquest it captured 4,000,000 barrels (640,000 m<sup>3</sup>) of oil (~5.5×10<sup>5</sup> tonnes) left behind by retreating Allied forces, and by 1943 was able to get production in the Dutch East Indies up to 50 million barrels (~6.8<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup> t), 76 per cent of its 1940 output rate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GSWW6_266_376-1"><a href="#cite_note-GSWW6_266-376">[374]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_fronts_and_production">Home fronts and production</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Military_production_during_World_War_II" title="Military production during World War II">Military production during World War II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Home_front_during_World_War_II" title="Home front during World War II">Home front during World War II</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WorldWarII-GDP-Relations-Allies-Axis-simple.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="820" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/WorldWarII-GDP-Relations-Allies-Axis-simple.svg/330px-WorldWarII-GDP-Relations-Allies-Axis-simple.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/WorldWarII-GDP-Relations-Allies-Axis-simple.svg/495px-WorldWarII-GDP-Relations-Allies-Axis-simple.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/WorldWarII-GDP-Relations-Allies-Axis-simple.svg/660px-WorldWarII-GDP-Relations-Allies-Axis-simple.svg.png 2x" width="330"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WorldWarII-GDP-Relations-Allies-Axis-simple.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Allied to Axis GDP ratio</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Europe, before the outbreak of the war, the Allies had significant advantages in both population and economics. In 1938, the Western Allies (United Kingdom, France, Poland and British Dominions) had a 30 per cent larger population and a 30 per cent higher gross domestic product than the European Axis powers (Germany and Italy); if colonies are included, it then gives the Allies more than a 5:1 advantage in population and nearly 2:1 advantage in GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6Econ3_377-0"><a href="#cite_note-6Econ3-377">[375]</a></sup> In Asia at the same time, China had roughly six times the population of Japan, but only an 89 per cent higher GDP; this is reduced to three times the population and only a 38 per cent higher GDP if Japanese colonies are included.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6Econ3_377-1"><a href="#cite_note-6Econ3-377">[375]</a></sup></p>
<p>The United States provided about two-thirds of all the ordnance used by the Allies in terms of warships, transports, warplanes, artillery, tanks, trucks, and ammunition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-378"><a href="#cite_note-378">[376]</a></sup> Though the Allies' economic and population advantages were largely mitigated during the initial rapid blitzkrieg attacks of Germany and Japan, they became the decisive factor by 1942, after the United States and Soviet Union joined the Allies, as the war largely settled into one of <a href="/wiki/Attrition_warfare" title="Attrition warfare">attrition</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6Econ2_379-0"><a href="#cite_note-6Econ2-379">[377]</a></sup> While the Allies' ability to out-produce the Axis is often attributed to the Allies having more access to natural resources, other factors, such as Germany and Japan's reluctance to employ women in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labour_force" title="Labour force">labour force</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-380"><a href="#cite_note-380">[378]</a></sup> Allied <a href="/wiki/Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II" title="Strategic bombing during World War II">strategic bombing</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-381"><a href="#cite_note-381">[379]</a></sup> and Germany's late shift to a <a href="/wiki/War_economy" title="War economy">war economy</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-382"><a href="#cite_note-382">[380]</a></sup> contributed significantly. Additionally, neither Germany nor Japan planned to fight a protracted war, and were not equipped to do so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-383"><a href="#cite_note-383">[381]</a></sup> To improve their production, Germany and Japan used millions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_labour" title="Slave labour">slave labourers</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-384"><a href="#cite_note-384">[382]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Forced_labour_under_German_rule_during_World_War_II" title="Forced labour under German rule during World War II">Germany used</a> about 12 million people, mostly from Eastern Europe,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-compensation_354-1"><a href="#cite_note-compensation-354">[352]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Japan" title="Slavery in Japan">Japan used</a> more than 18 million people in Far East Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zhifen2002_362-1"><a href="#cite_note-zhifen2002-362">[360]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indonesiaww2_363-1"><a href="#cite_note-indonesiaww2-363">[361]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Advances_in_technology_and_warfare">Advances in technology and warfare</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Technology_during_World_War_II" title="Technology during World War II">Technology during World War II</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Boeing-Whichata_B-29_Assembly_Line_-_1944.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="783" data-file-width="1024" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Boeing-Whichata_B-29_Assembly_Line_-_1944.jpg/225px-Boeing-Whichata_B-29_Assembly_Line_-_1944.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Boeing-Whichata_B-29_Assembly_Line_-_1944.jpg/338px-Boeing-Whichata_B-29_Assembly_Line_-_1944.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Boeing-Whichata_B-29_Assembly_Line_-_1944.jpg/450px-Boeing-Whichata_B-29_Assembly_Line_-_1944.jpg 2x" width="225"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Boeing-Whichata_B-29_Assembly_Line_-_1944.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Boeing_B-29_Superfortress" title="Boeing B-29 Superfortress">B-29 Superfortress</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strategic_bombers" title="Strategic bombers">strategic bombers</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a> assembly line in <a href="/wiki/Wichita,_Kansas" title="Wichita, Kansas">Wichita, Kansas</a>, 1944</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Aircraft were used for <a href="/wiki/Reconnaissance_aircraft" title="Reconnaissance aircraft">reconnaissance</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Fighter_aircraft" title="Fighter aircraft">fighters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bomber" title="Bomber">bombers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Close_air_support" title="Close air support">ground-support</a>, and each role was advanced considerably. Innovation included <a href="/wiki/Airlift" title="Airlift">airlift</a> (the capability to quickly move limited high-priority supplies, equipment, and personnel);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EncWWII_76_385-0"><a href="#cite_note-EncWWII_76-385">[383]</a></sup> and of <a href="/wiki/Strategic_bombing" title="Strategic bombing">strategic bombing</a> (the bombing of enemy industrial and population centres to destroy the enemy's ability to wage war).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-386"><a href="#cite_note-386">[384]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Anti-aircraft_warfare" title="Anti-aircraft warfare">Anti-aircraft weaponry</a> also advanced, including defences such as <a href="/wiki/Radar" title="Radar">radar</a> and surface-to-air artillery, such as the German <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/88_mm_gun" title="88 mm gun">88 mm gun</a>. The use of the <a href="/wiki/Jet_aircraft" title="Jet aircraft">jet aircraft</a> was pioneered and, though late introduction meant it had little impact, it led to jets becoming standard in air forces worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-387"><a href="#cite_note-387">[385]</a></sup></p>
<p>Advances were made in nearly every aspect of <a href="/wiki/Naval_warfare" title="Naval warfare">naval warfare</a>, most notably with aircraft carriers and submarines. Although <a href="/wiki/Aeronautics" title="Aeronautics">aeronautical</a> warfare had relatively little success at the start of the war, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Taranto" title="Battle of Taranto">actions at Taranto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Coral_Sea" title="Battle of the Coral Sea">Coral Sea</a> established the carrier as the dominant capital ship in place of the battleship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EncWWII_163_388-0"><a href="#cite_note-EncWWII_163-388">[386]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-389"><a href="#cite_note-389">[387]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-390"><a href="#cite_note-390">[388]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the Atlantic, <a href="/wiki/Escort_carrier" title="Escort carrier">escort carriers</a> proved to be a vital part of Allied convoys, increasing the effective protection radius and helping to close the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_gap" title="Mid-Atlantic gap">Mid-Atlantic gap</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-391"><a href="#cite_note-391">[389]</a></sup> Carriers were also more economical than battleships because of the relatively low cost of aircraft<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-392"><a href="#cite_note-392">[390]</a></sup> and their not requiring to be as heavily armoured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-393"><a href="#cite_note-393">[391]</a></sup> Submarines, which had proved to be an effective weapon during the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bur.26Ryd_1995_15_394-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bur.26Ryd_1995_15-394">[392]</a></sup> were anticipated by all sides to be important in the second. The British focused development on <a href="/wiki/Anti-submarine_warfare" title="Anti-submarine warfare">anti-submarine</a> <a href="/wiki/Anti-submarine_weapon" title="Anti-submarine weapon">weaponry</a> and tactics, such as <a href="/wiki/Sonar" title="Sonar">sonar</a> and convoys, while Germany focused on improving its offensive capability, with designs such as the <a href="/wiki/German_Type_VII_submarine" title="German Type VII submarine">Type VII submarine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wolfpack_(naval_tactic)" title="Wolfpack (naval tactic)">wolfpack</a> tactics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bur.26Ryd_1995_16_395-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bur.26Ryd_1995_16-395">[393]</a></sup> Gradually, improving Allied technologies such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leigh_light" title="Leigh light">Leigh light</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hedgehog_(weapon)" title="Hedgehog (weapon)">hedgehog</a>, <a href="/wiki/Squid_(weapon)" title="Squid (weapon)">squid</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mark_24_mine" title="Mark 24 mine">homing torpedoes</a> proved victorious.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_141-1880,_Peenem%C3%BCnde,_Start_einer_V2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="784" data-file-width="600" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Bundesarchiv_Bild_141-1880%2C_Peenem%C3%BCnde%2C_Start_einer_V2.jpg/200px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_141-1880%2C_Peenem%C3%BCnde%2C_Start_einer_V2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Bundesarchiv_Bild_141-1880%2C_Peenem%C3%BCnde%2C_Start_einer_V2.jpg/300px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_141-1880%2C_Peenem%C3%BCnde%2C_Start_einer_V2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Bundesarchiv_Bild_141-1880%2C_Peenem%C3%BCnde%2C_Start_einer_V2.jpg/400px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_141-1880%2C_Peenem%C3%BCnde%2C_Start_einer_V2.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_141-1880,_Peenem%C3%BCnde,_Start_einer_V2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/V-2_rocket" title="V-2 rocket">V-2 rocket</a> launched from a fixed site in <a href="/wiki/Peenem%C3%BCnde" title="Peenemünde">Peenemünde</a>, 21 June 1943</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Land_warfare" title="Land warfare">Land warfare</a> changed from the static front lines of World War I to increased mobility and <a href="/wiki/Combined_arms" title="Combined arms">combined arms</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Tank" title="Tank">tank</a>, which had been used predominantly for infantry support in the First World War, had evolved into the primary weapon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EncWWII_125_396-0"><a href="#cite_note-EncWWII_125-396">[394]</a></sup> In the late 1930s, tank design was considerably more advanced than it had been during World War I,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-397"><a href="#cite_note-397">[395]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tanks_in_World_War_II" title="Tanks in World War II">advances continued throughout the war</a> with increases in speed, armour and firepower.</p>
<p>At the start of the war, most commanders thought enemy tanks should be met by tanks with superior specifications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EncWWII_108_398-0"><a href="#cite_note-EncWWII_108-398">[396]</a></sup> This idea was challenged by the poor performance of the relatively light early tank guns against armour, and German doctrine of avoiding tank-versus-tank combat. This, along with Germany's use of combined arms, were among the key elements of their highly successful blitzkrieg tactics across Poland and France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EncWWII_125_396-1"><a href="#cite_note-EncWWII_125-396">[394]</a></sup> Many means of <a href="/wiki/Anti-tank_warfare" title="Anti-tank warfare">destroying tanks</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Indirect_fire" title="Indirect fire">indirect artillery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anti-tank_gun" title="Anti-tank gun">anti-tank guns</a> (both towed and <a href="/wiki/Self-propelled_gun" title="Self-propelled gun">self-propelled</a>), <a href="/wiki/Anti-tank_mine" title="Anti-tank mine">mines</a>, short-ranged infantry antitank weapons, and other tanks were utilised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EncWWII_108_398-1"><a href="#cite_note-EncWWII_108-398">[396]</a></sup> Even with large-scale mechanisation, infantry remained the backbone of all forces,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EncWWII_734_399-0"><a href="#cite_note-EncWWII_734-399">[397]</a></sup> and throughout the war, most infantry were equipped similarly to World War I.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Comp_221_400-0"><a href="#cite_note-Comp_221-400">[398]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trinity_device_readied.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4371" data-file-width="5520" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Trinity_device_readied.jpg/225px-Trinity_device_readied.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Trinity_device_readied.jpg/338px-Trinity_device_readied.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Trinity_device_readied.jpg/450px-Trinity_device_readied.jpg 2x" width="225"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trinity_device_readied.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Nuclear <i>Gadget</i> being raised to the top of the detonation "shot tower", at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alamogordo_Bombing_and_Gunnery_Range" title="Alamogordo Bombing and Gunnery Range">Alamogordo Bombing Range</a>; <a href="/wiki/Trinity_(nuclear_test)" title="Trinity (nuclear test)">Trinity nuclear test</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>, July 1945</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The portable machine gun spread, a notable example being the German <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MG34" title="MG34">MG34</a>, and various <a href="/wiki/Submachine_gun" title="Submachine gun">submachine guns</a> which were suited to <a href="/wiki/Close_combat" title="Close combat">close combat</a> in urban and jungle settings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Comp_221_400-1"><a href="#cite_note-Comp_221-400">[398]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Assault_rifle" title="Assault rifle">assault rifle</a>, a late war development incorporating many features of the rifle and submachine gun, became the standard postwar infantry weapon for most armed forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-401"><a href="#cite_note-401">[399]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-402"><a href="#cite_note-402">[400]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most major belligerents attempted to solve the problems of complexity and security involved in using large <a href="/wiki/Codebook" title="Codebook">codebooks</a> for <a href="/wiki/Cryptography" title="Cryptography">cryptography</a> by designing <a href="/wiki/Cipher" title="Cipher">ciphering</a> machines, the most well known being the German <a href="/wiki/Enigma_machine" title="Enigma machine">Enigma machine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-403"><a href="#cite_note-403">[401]</a></sup> Development of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SIGINT" title="SIGINT">SIGINT</a> (<i>sig</i>nals <i>int</i>elligence) and <a href="/wiki/Cryptanalysis" title="Cryptanalysis">cryptanalysis</a> enabled the countering process of decryption. Notable examples were the Allied decryption of <a href="/wiki/Japanese_naval_codes" title="Japanese naval codes">Japanese naval codes</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schoenherr_404-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schoenherr-404">[402]</a></sup> and British <a href="/wiki/Ultra" title="Ultra">Ultra</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Bombe#The_British_Bombe" title="Bombe">pioneering method</a> for decoding Enigma benefiting from information given to Britain by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_Cipher_Bureau#Gift_to_allies" title="Polish Cipher Bureau">Polish Cipher Bureau</a>, which had been decoding early versions of Enigma before the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-405"><a href="#cite_note-405">[403]</a></sup> Another aspect of <a href="/wiki/Military_intelligence" title="Military intelligence">military intelligence</a> was the use of <a href="/wiki/Deception" title="Deception">deception</a>, which the Allies used to great effect, such as in operations <a href="/wiki/Operation_Mincemeat" title="Operation Mincemeat">Mincemeat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Bodyguard" title="Operation Bodyguard">Bodyguard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schoenherr_404-1"><a href="#cite_note-Schoenherr-404">[402]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-406"><a href="#cite_note-406">[404]</a></sup> Other technological and engineering feats achieved during, or as a result of, the war include the world's first programmable computers (<a href="/wiki/Z3_(computer)" title="Z3 (computer)">Z3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colossus_computer" title="Colossus computer">Colossus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/ENIAC" title="ENIAC">ENIAC</a>), <a href="/wiki/V-1_flying_bomb" title="V-1 flying bomb">guided missiles</a> and <a href="/wiki/V-2_rocket" title="V-2 rocket">modern rockets</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Project" title="Manhattan Project">Manhattan Project</a>'s development of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear weapons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Operations_research" title="Operations research">operations research</a> and the development of <a href="/wiki/Mulberry_harbour" title="Mulberry harbour">artificial harbours</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Pluto" title="Operation Pluto">oil pipelines under the English Channel</a>.</p>

<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Wars_(miniseries)" title="The World Wars (miniseries)">The World Wars (miniseries)</a></i> The World Wars is a three-part, six-hour event miniseries by the History Channel that premiered on Monday, 26 May 2014, (Memorial Day) airing for three consecutive nights. An extended version of the series with never before seen footage was subsequently broadcast on H2 and in more than 160 countries on 22 June 2014</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Apocalypse:_The_Second_World_War" title="Apocalypse: The Second World War">Apocalypse: The Second World War</a></i> (2009), a six-part French documentary by Daniel Costelle and Isabelle Clarke about World War II</li>

<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_World_at_War" title="The World at War">The World at War</a></i> (1974), a 26-part <a href="/wiki/Thames_Television" title="Thames Television">Thames Television</a> series that covers most aspects of World War II from many points of view. It includes interviews with many key figures including <a href="/wiki/Karl_D%C3%B6nitz" title="Karl Dönitz">Karl Dönitz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Speer" title="Albert Speer">Albert Speer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Eden" title="Anthony Eden">Anthony Eden</a>.</li>
</ul>

<li id="cite_note-Keegan_1997_35-68"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Keegan_1997_35_68-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFKeegan1997">Keegan 1997</a>, p. 35.<br/>
<a href="#CITEREFCienciala2010">Cienciala 2010</a>, p. 128, observes that, while it is true that Poland was far away, making it difficult for the French and British to provide support, "[f]ew Western historians of World War II ... know that the British had committed to bomb Germany if it attacked Poland, but did not do so except for one raid on the base of Wilhelmshafen. The French, who committed to attack Germany in the west, had no intention of doing so."</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-USAWWIIcp4-161"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-USAWWIIcp4_161-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-USAWWIIcp4_161-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://www.ibiblio.org/hyperwar/USA/USA-WD-Strategic1/USA-WD-Strategic1-4.html" rel="nofollow">"The Showdown With Japan Aug–Dec 1941"</a>. <i>US Army in WWII – Strategic Planning for Coalition Warfare</i>. pp. 63–96.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AWorld+War+II&amp;rft.atitle=The+Showdown+With+Japan+Aug%E2%80%93Dec+1941&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=US+Army+in+WWII+%E2%80%93+Strategic+Planning+for+Coalition+Warfare&amp;rft.pages=63-96&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.ibiblio.org%2Fhyperwar%2FUSA%2FUSA-WD-Strategic1%2FUSA-WD-Strategic1-4.html&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-162"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-162">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="http://www.ibiblio.org/pha/pha/congress/app-d.html#363" rel="nofollow">The United States Replies</a>. Investigation of the Pearl Harbor attack.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-163"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-163">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFPainter2012">Painter 2012</a>, p. 26: "The United States cut off oil exports to Japan in the summer of 1941, forcing Japanese leaders to choose between going to war to seize the oil fields of the Netherlands East Indies or giving in to U.S. pressure."<br/>
<a href="#CITEREFWood2007">Wood 2007</a>, p. 9, listing various military and diplomatic developments, observes that "the threat to Japan was not purely economic."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTELightbody2004125-164"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTELightbody2004125_164-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFLightbody2004">Lightbody 2004</a>, p. 125.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-165"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-165">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFWeinberg2005">Weinberg 2005</a>, p. 310; <a href="#CITEREFDower1986">Dower 1986</a>, p. 5, calls attention to the fact that "the Allied struggle against Japan exposed the racist underpinnings of the European and American colonial structure. Japan did not invade independent countries in southern Asia. It invaded colonial outposts which the Westerners had dominated for generations, taking absolutely for granted their racial and cultural superiority over their Asian subjects." Dower goes on to note that, before the horrors of Japanese occupation made themselves felt, many Asians responded favourably to the victories of the Imperial Japanese forces.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEWood200711.E2.80.932-166"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWood200711.E2.80.932_166-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFWood2007">Wood 2007</a>, pp. 11–2.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEWohlstetter1962341.E2.80.933-167"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWohlstetter1962341.E2.80.933_167-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWohlstetter1962341.E2.80.933_167-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFWohlstetter1962">Wohlstetter 1962</a>, pp. 341–3.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-168"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-168">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFDunn1998">Dunn 1998</a>, p. 157. According to <a href="#CITEREFMay1955">May 1955</a>, p. 155, Churchill stated: "Russian declaration of war on Japan would be greatly to our advantage, provided, but only provided, that Russians are confident that will not impair their Western Front."</span></li>

But when this didn't happen he desperately attempted to call off his bargain with Eisenhower, who cut short the matter on 8 September by announcing news of its existence. The next day the hero of Abyssinia, his king, and a small retinue deserted Rome for the southeast tip of Italy, leaving most of Italy to the Nazis."</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-Chubarov_2001_122-243"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Chubarov_2001_122_243-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFChubarov2001">Chubarov 2001</a>, p. 122.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-244"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-244">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFHolland2008">Holland 2008</a>, pp. 169–84; <a href="#CITEREFBeevor2012">Beevor 2012</a>, pp. 568–73.<br/>
The weeks after the fall of Rome saw a dramatic upswing in German atrocities in Italy (<a href="#CITEREFMazower2008">Mazower 2008</a>, pp. 500–2). The period featured massacres with victims in the hundreds at <a href="/wiki/Civitella_in_Val_di_Chiana" title="Civitella in Val di Chiana">Civitella</a> (<a href="#CITEREFde_GraziaPaggi1991">de Grazia &amp; Paggi 1991</a>; <a href="#CITEREFBelco2010">Belco 2010</a>), <a href="/wiki/Ardeatine_massacre" title="Ardeatine massacre">Fosse Ardeatine</a> (<a href="#CITEREFPortelli2003">Portelli 2003</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Sant%27Anna_di_Stazzema_massacre" title="Sant'Anna di Stazzema massacre">Sant'Anna di Stazzema</a> (<a href="#CITEREFGordon2012">Gordon 2012</a>, pp. 10–1), and is capped with the <a href="/wiki/Marzabotto_massacre" title="Marzabotto massacre">Marzabotto massacre</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Lightbody_2004_224-245"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Lightbody_2004_224_245-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFLightbody2004">Lightbody 2004</a>, p. 224.</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-401"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-401">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://greyfalcon.us/Infantry%20Weapons%20Of%20World%20War%202.htm" rel="nofollow">"Infantry Weapons Of World War 2"</a>. Grey Falcon (Black Sun)<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">14 November</span> 2009</span>. <q>These all-purpose guns were developed and used by the German army in the 2nd half of World War 2 as a result of studies which showed that the ordinary rifle's long range is much longer than needed, since the soldiers almost always fired at enemies closer than half of its effective range. The assault rifle is a balanced compromise between the rifle and the sub-machine gun, having sufficient range and accuracy to be used as a rifle, combined with the rapid-rate automatic firepower of the sub machine gun. Thanks to these combined advantages, assault rifles such as the American M-16 and the Russian AK-47 are the basic weapon of the modern soldier</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AWorld+War+II&amp;rft.btitle=Infantry+Weapons+Of+World+War+2&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.pub=Grey+Falcon+%28Black+Sun%29&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fgreyfalcon.us%2FInfantry%2520Weapons%2520Of%2520World%2520War%25202.htm&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
